Counting Verses/Tasbih with the Hand in Prayer: Ruling and Proofs
Explains ruling and proofs for counting verses/tasbih with hand in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on counting verses or tasbih with the hand during prayer, identify the proofs from the Salaf, and explain why it is makruh tanzih.

Core Idea
Counting verses or tasbih with the hand during prayer is makruh tanzih because it involves unnecessary action that distracts from khushu.

This lesson addresses a common practice: counting verses or tasbih with the hand while in prayer. The Hanafi school classifies this as makruh tanzih (slightly disliked) because it entails a slight action (amal qalil) that can distract the heart from devotion. We examine the proofs from the practice of the early Muslims that lead to this ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the hukm level for counting verses/tasbih with the hand during prayer. The text says it is makruh (disliked). Determine the category: makruh tanzih, not tahrimi.
The ruling differs inside vs outside prayer.
2
Identify the condition
Note the distinction: outside prayer it is permissible; inside prayer it becomes makruh due to the action required.
The key factor is the location (prayer vs non-prayer).
3
Locate the proofs
Find the dalil from the source: the athar of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz and Ibn Mas'ud avoiding counting, and the practice of Abu Hurayra using pebbles outside prayer.
The proofs are from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
4
Understand the reasoning
Explain why it is disliked: it involves amal qalil (a small action) that distracts the heart from khushu.
Amal qalil does not invalidate prayer but is discouraged.
5
Note the exception
Using pebbles or date stones for tasbih outside prayer is permissible, as shown by the companions. But inside prayer, even that is disliked if it involves movement.
The exception applies to the method, not the location.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۷۱) وعد الآى والتسبيح باليد
ترجمه : (۵۷۱) ہاتھ سے آیت اور تسبیح گننا۔
تشریح : نماز سے باہر ہاتھ سے تسبیح گننا جائز ہے، البتہ نماز کے اندر ہاتھ سے آیت یا تسبیح گئے گا تو عمل قلیل لازم آئے گا اور دل اس میں مشغول ہوگا اس لئے یہ مکروہ ہے۔
وجه : (۱) سأله عمر بن عبد العزيز تعد الآية فى الصلاة ؟ فقال ما افعل قال و انا ايضا ما افعل (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ۳۱۱ من کرهه ، ج اول ص ۴۲۷، نمبر ۴۹۱۰) (۲) كان عبد الله يكره العدد و يقول : أيمن على اللــه حسـنـاتـه ـ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ۶۷۵ من کره عقد التسی ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۶۴ نمبر ۷۶۶۶ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ انگلیوں سے تسبیح گنا مکروہ ہے۔ اس لئے نماز میں بھی مکروہ ہوگا۔ (۳) کنکری یا دھاگے کی تبیج استعمال کرے اس کے لئے یہ عمل صحابی ہے. قال نزلت على ابى هريرة و معه كيس في حصى او نوى فيقول سبحان الله سبحان الله حتى ا اذا نفذ ما في الكيس القاه الى جارية سوداء فجمعته ثم دفعته اليه - ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب في عقد التسبیح وعد الحصی ، ج ثانی ص ۱۶۳ نمبر ۷۶۶۰) اس عمل صحابی میں ہے کہ کنکری اور گٹھلی سے تسبیح گن سکتا ہے۔ (۴) عن حکیم بن الدیلمی عن مولاة لسعد ان سعدا كان يسبح بالحصى و النوى - (مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ، باب في عقد التسبیح وعدد الحصی ، ج ثانی ص ۱۶۳، نمبر (۷۶۵۸)
(571) Counting verses and tasbih with the hand. Translation: (571) Counting verses and tasbih with the hand. Explanation: Counting tasbih with the hand outside of prayer is permissible. However, inside the prayer, if one counts verses or tasbih with the hand, a little action (amal qalil) will be required and the heart will be occupied, so it is disliked. Proof: (1) 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz asked: 'Do you count verses in prayer?' He said: 'I do not do it.' He said: 'I also do not do it.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab 311: Man karihahu, vol. 1, p. 427, no. 4910) (2) 'Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud) disliked counting and said: 'I do not count my good deeds against Allah.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab 675: Man kariha 'aqd al-tasbih, vol. 2, p. 164, no. 7666) From this athar, it is understood that counting tasbih with the fingers is disliked. Therefore, it is also disliked in prayer. (3) As for using pebbles or a thread for tasbih, there is this action of a Companion: He (Abu Hurayra) said: I descended upon Abu Hurayra while he had a bag of pebbles or date stones, and he would say 'Subhan Allah, Subhan Allah' until what was in the bag was finished, then he would throw it to a black slave girl who would collect it and return it to him. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab fi 'aqd al-tasbih wa 'adad al-hasa, vol. 2, p. 163, no. 7660) This action shows that one can count tasbih with pebbles and date stones. (4) From Hakim ibn al-Daylami from the freed slave of Sa'd that Sa'd used to do tasbih with pebbles and date stones. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab fi 'aqd al-tasbih wa 'adad al-hasa, vol. 2, p. 163, no. 7658)
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning counting verses or tasbih with the hand during prayer. The matn states: (571) Counting verses and tasbih with the hand. The author explains that outside of prayer, using the hand to count tasbih is permissible (ja'iz). However, inside the prayer, if one counts verses or tasbih by moving the fingers or hand, it involves a slight action (amal qalil) and distracts the heart, making it disliked (makruh). The proofs (wajh) are from the actions of the early Muslims: (1) 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz was asked about counting verses in prayer, and he said he does not do it, indicating its dislike. (2) 'Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud) disliked counting with fingers and said he does not count his good deeds against Allah. From this, the author deduces that counting with fingers is disliked, and since prayer requires focus, it is disliked during prayer. (3) However, counting tasbih with pebbles or date stones is permissible, as shown by the action of Abu Hurayra and Sa'd. This indicates that using inanimate objects for counting is acceptable outside prayer, but inside prayer it is still disliked because of the movement. The Hanafi school holds that any unnecessary movement with the hand or counting during prayer that disrupts concentration is makruh tanzihi. The use of a tasbih (prayer beads) outside prayer is permissible, but inside prayer it is disliked. The authority weight is from the narrations (athar) of the Companions and successors, so it is based on practice.

Key Terms
تسبیح (tasbih): Saying 'Subhan Allah' or counting glorifications; also used for prayer beads
عمل قلیل (amal qalil): A small action that does not invalidate prayer but is discouraged
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; a category between mubah and haram, here tanzihi (not severely disliked)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is counting verses or tasbih with the hand during prayer considered makruh in the Hanafi school?
A) It invalidates the prayer
B) It involves unnecessary action and distracts the heart
C) It is considered showing off
D) It is only permissible outside the mosque

Key Takeaway
Counting verses or tasbih with the hand during prayer is makruh tanzih due to the distraction it causes; avoid it to preserve khushu.

Imam Standing Alone in the Mihrab: Ruling and Conditions
Ruling on imam's position in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the imam standing alone in the mihrab and identify the condition that triggers the dislikedness.

Core Idea
The imam should not stand away from the row when space is available.

This lesson examines a specific rule of congregational prayer: the imam's position relative to the rows. The matn states that it is disliked for the imam to stand alone in the mihrab, on an elevated place, or any isolated spot when there is empty space in the row. This ruling reinforces the value of unity in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act being discussed is the imam standing alone in a mihrab (a niche or elevated place) during congregational prayer.
2
State the ruling
Determine the hukm level for this act according to the Hanafi school.
The text indicates it is makruh (disliked), specifically makruh tanzihi.
3
Find the condition
Identify the condition that makes the act disliked. The phrase 'while there is space in the row' is key.
If the row is full or the imam has a valid reason, the dislikedness may not apply.
4
Understand the wisdom
Consider why this ruling exists. It promotes unity and avoids isolation of the imam from the congregation.
Some earlier scholars mention resemblance to non-Muslim practices, but the main reason is maintaining row continuity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۷۲ [الف] وقيام الامام فى المحراب او على مكان او الارض
ترجمه : (۵۷۲ ( الف ))) امام کا محراب میں، یا اونچی جگہ میں، یا کسی خاص جگہ میں تنہا کھڑا ہونا ،صف میں جگہ ہوتے ہوئے
(572[a]) The imam standing in the mihrab, or on a raised place, or on the ground. Translation: (572(a)) The imam standing in the mihrab, or on an elevated place, or in a specific place alone, while there is space in the row.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement (matn) from a Hanafi fiqh work. It lists another disliked act (makruh) for the one praying, specifically for the imam. The matn states: (572[a]) The imam standing in the mihrab, or on a raised place, or on the ground (alone). The Urdu translation explains: The imam standing alone in the mihrab, or on an elevated place, or in a specific place, while there is space in the congregation row. The ruling is that it is disliked for the imam to stand separate from the congregation when there is room in the row to join. This is because it goes against the unity of the congregation and may resemble the practice of non-Muslims or create disunity. The Hanafi school considers this as makruh tanzihi. The full proof is not given in this excerpt, but the ruling is clear. The text uses the phrase 'while there is space in the row' — meaning if the imam stands alone despite there being empty space in the row, it is disliked; but if the row is full or there is a valid reason (such as the mihrab being the sunna position), it may be permissible. However, the explicit ruling here is absolute dislike when space exists.

Key Terms
محراب (mihrab): A niche in the mosque wall indicating the qibla, where the imam stands
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; here tanzihi (slightly disliked)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it makruh for the imam to stand alone in the mihrab?
A) Always
B) When there is empty space in the congregation row
C) Only during Fajr prayer
D) When the mihrab is made of stone

Key Takeaway
The imam standing alone in the mihrab is disliked (makruh tanzih) only when there is empty space in the row; otherwise it is permissible.

Ruling on Prayer When Food is Present and Hungry
States the ruling on prayer with food present and hunger disturbing focus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying when food is present and hungry, and identify the two hadith proofs that support this ruling.

Core Idea
Praying when food is present and hunger disturbs khushu is makruh tanzih — not invalid.

This lesson addresses a practical conflict: the desire to eat versus the obligation to pray. The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling based on the worshipper's concentration (khushu). We will examine the hadith evidence and understand why the prayer remains valid but disliked in such a state.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying when food is present and the worshipper is hungry enough that it disturbs khushu. The Hanafi ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked, not sinful).
If hunger does not disturb khushu, it is not makruh.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: one from Aisha (ra) narrated by Muslim, and one from Ibn Umar (ra) narrated by Bukhari.
The hadith texts are quoted partially in the source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The negation 'لا صلاة' in the first hadith indicates prohibition; Hanafis interpret this as makruh, not batil. The imperative 'لا يعجل' in the second hadith permits delaying prayer to finish eating.
These proofs are zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may not consider it makruh if one can maintain focus despite hunger.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is makruh tanzih, based on the hadith and the importance of khushu.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل ما يكره للمصلى
تشريح : كھانا موجود ہو اور اتنی بھوک لگی ہو کہ دل ادھر مائل ہو جائے اور نماز میں خشوع خضوع ختم ہو جائے ، ایسی صورت میں اور نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے، اور بھوک زیادہ نہ لگی ہوتو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔
وجه : (۱) بھوک تیز ہونے کے وقت نماز مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ قالت عائشة ) اجلس يا غندر انى سمعت رسول الله الله يقول لا صلاة بحضرة الطعام ولا هو يدافعه الاخبثان (مسلم شریف ، باب کراھة الصلاة بحضرة الطعام ، الخ، ص ۲۲۶، نمبر ۱۲۴۶/۵۶۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کھانے کے وقت نماز نہ پڑھے۔ (۲) پہلے کھانا کھائے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال قال النبى الله اذا كان احدكم على الطعام فلا يعجل حتى يقضي حاجته منه و ان اقيمت الصلاة - ( بخاری شریف ، باب اذ احضر الطعام واقیمت الصلاۃ ص ۱۰۹، نمبر ۶۷۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کھانے یا پیشاب پینانے کی ضرورت ہو تو پہلے اس کو پوری کرو چاہے اقامت کہی جارہی ہو۔
لغت : بذلته : خرچ، یاب البذلة : ایسا کپڑا جس میں آدمی محنت مزدوری کرتا ہو۔ تذلل : ذلیل ہونا ، آہ وزاری کرنا۔ التضرع: گڑ گڑانا۔ البال: دل، ایشغل البال: جو دل کو مشغول کرے۔
Section: What is disliked for the one praying. Explanation: Food is present and one is so hungry that the heart inclines towards it and concentration and humility in prayer disappear; in such a situation, praying is makruh. If hunger is not severe, it is not makruh. Evidence: (1) Prayer at the time of intense hunger is makruh; for this there is this hadith: Aisha (ra) said, 'Sit down, O Ghundar, for I heard the Messenger of Allah (saw) say: There is no prayer when food is present, nor when one is suppressing the two filths.' (Muslim). This hadith indicates that one should not pray at the time of food. (2) One should eat first; for this there is this hadith: Ibn Umar (ra) narrated that the Prophet (saw) said: 'When any of you is at food, let him not hasten until he fulfills his need from it, even if the prayer is established.' (Bukhari). This hadith indicates that if one needs food or to relieve himself, he should complete that first even if the iqamah is being said. Vocabulary: بذلته: expenditure; یاب البذلة: a garment in which a person does labor; تذلل: humiliation, beseeching; التضرع: supplication; البال: heart, ایشغل البال: that which occupies the heart.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage opens the section on disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer. The author first addresses the situation where food is present and the worshipper is hungry enough that it disturbs the concentration (khushu) of prayer. According to the Hanafi school, praying in such a state is makruh tanzih (reprehensible but not sinful). The author provides two hadith proofs: one from Aisha (ra) reporting the Prophet’s (saw) prohibition of prayer when food is served, and another from Ibn Umar (ra) instructing to finish eating before praying, even if the congregation has begun. The vocabulary list at the end explains key Arabic terms used in the hadiths, such as 'تذلل' meaning humility and 'البال' meaning heart or mind. The overall ruling is that one should prioritize eating when hungry to ensure proper focus in prayer.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): An act that is disliked and discouraged; performing it is blameworthy but not sinful. In Hanafi, it is a distinct category between mubah and haram.
خشوع (khushu): Concentration and humility in prayer, a state of the heart required for proper fulfillment.
لا صلاة (la salata): A negation phrase used in hadith; in this context, it indicates prohibition rather than invalidity according to Hanafi interpretation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying when food is present and one is very hungry?
A) The prayer is invalid (batil)
B) The prayer is makruh (disliked)
C) The prayer is valid and there is no dislike
D) The prayer must be postponed until after eating

Key Takeaway
Prayer when hungry and food is present is makruh tanzih; one should prioritize eating to achieve khushu, but the prayer remains valid.

Ruling on Imam Standing in the Mihrab or on an Elevated Place
Details the disliked actions of the imam standing alone in the mihrab or on an elevated spot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the imam standing alone in the mihrab or on a raised place, identify the evidence that makes it makruh, and distinguish between invalid and merely disliked actions.

Core Idea
The imam must not stand higher than the congregation or alone in the mihrab — it is makruh.

This lesson examines the rulings related to the imam's placement during congregational prayer. The Hanafi school rules that it is makruh tanzihi for the imam to stand alone in the mihrab (prayer niche) or on any raised platform, as this resembles the practices of Jews and Christians and contradicts the spirit of humility in prayer. We will explore the textual evidence from hadith and the reasoning behind this ruling, as well as the related issue of leaving gaps in the rows.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The passage covers three scenarios: (1) imam standing alone in the mihrab, (2) imam standing alone on an elevated place, and (3) a person leaving a gap in the row. For each, the ruling is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites multiple proofs: an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, a hadith from Musa al-Juhani warning against mihrabs like Christians, a hadith from Hudhayfah prohibiting the imam from standing higher than the congregation, and hadiths about completing the rows from Anas ibn Malik.
These are all ahad or athar, giving zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith 'When a man leads people, he should not stand in a place higher than theirs' explicitly prohibits elevation. The warning against mihrabs of Christians indicates resemblance to non-Muslims is the reason. The command to complete rows shows that gaps are disliked.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools allow the imam to be elevated if needed for visibility. The Hanafi position is more precautionary, avoiding resemblance to non-Muslims.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that it is makruh tanzihi. The prayer remains valid, but the action distracts from humility and should be avoided.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۷۲ ( الف ))، امام کا محراب میں ، یا اونچی جگہ میں، یا کسی خاص جگہ میں تنہا کھڑا ہونا ،صف میں جگہ ہوتے ہوئے پیچھے کھڑا ہونا۔
تشریح : امام تنہا محراب میں کھڑا ہو، یا اونچی جگہ میں کھڑا ہو، یا کسی خاص جگہ میں کھڑا ہو اور اس کے ساتھ کوئی آدمی نہ ہو، جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہو کہ وہ بالکل الگ تھلگ ہیں تو یہ مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ یہودیوں کی طرح الگ شان شوکت والا معلوم ہوتا ہے ۔ دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ صف میں جگہ ہوتے ہوئے بغیر مجبوری کے آدمی پیچھے کھڑا ہو جائے تو یہ بھی مکروہ ہے
وجه : (۱) عن ابراهيم كان يكره أن يصلى في طاق الامام - (مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب صلوۃ الامام فی الطاق ، ج ثانی ص ۲۷۴، نمبر ۳۹۱ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۲۷۸ الصلوۃ فی الطاق ، ج اول ،ص ۴۰۹، نمبر ۴۶۹۷ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ امام طاق یعنی محراب میں ہو تو یہ مکروہ ہے۔ البتہ امام محراب سے باہر ہو اور سجدہ محراب کے اندر کرتا ہو، تو چونکہ اس صورت میں امام کی کوئی خصوصیت نہیں رہی اسلئے یہ جائز ہے۔ (۲) عن موسى الجهني قال : قال رسول الله الا الله لا تزال هذه الامة أو قال أمتى بخير ما لم يتخذوا في مساجدهم مدائح كمدائح النصارى . (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ۲۷۸ الصلوة في الطاق، جاول، ص ۴۰۹، نمبر ۴۶۹۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مسجدوں میں نصاری کی طرح محراب بنانا اچھی بات نہیں ہے۔ مدائح کا معنی ہے، محراب (۳) أنه كان مع عمار بن ياسر بالمدائن .... قال له حذيفة : ألم تسمع رسول الله عله يقول : اذا أم الرجل القوم فلا يقم فى مكان أرفع من مقامهم . أو نحو ذالک قال عمار: لذالك اتبعتك حين أخذت عـلـى يـدی ۔ (ابوداود شریف ، باب الامام يقوم مكانا ارفع من مكان القوم ص ۱۹۸ نمبر ۵۹۸ مستدرک للحاکم ، باب و من کتاب الامامۃ وصلاة الجماعة ، ج اول ،ص ۳۲۹، نمبر ۷۶۰ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ امام اونچی جگہ پر ہو اور مقتدی نیچی جگہ پر ہو یہ اچھا نہیں ہے، اسی طرح اکیلا امام بیچی جگہ پر ہو تو اس میں امام کی توہین ہے اسلئے یہ بھی مکروہ ہے۔ (۴) پہلی صف پوری کرو اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے . عن انس ان رسول الله له قال أتموا الصف المقدم ثم الذين يليه فما كان من نقص فليكن في الصف الموخر ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب تسویۃ الصفوف ،ص ۱۰۵، نمبر (۶۷) ان دونوں حدیثوں میں ہے کہ پہلی صف پوری کریں (۵) عن انس قال قال رسول الله الله أتموا الصفوف فاني أراكم خلف ظهری (مسلم شریف، باب الصفوف تسوية الصفوف واقامتها، الخ، ص۱۸۴، نمبر ۹۷۶/۴۳۴)
Translation (572(a)): The imam standing in the mihrab, or on an elevated place, or in a specific place alone, or standing behind while there is space in the row. Explanation: If the imam stands alone in the mihrab, or on a raised place, or in a specific place with no one with him, giving the impression that he is completely isolated, then this is makruh. Because it resembles the Jews who appear with separate grandeur. Secondly, if a person stands behind a row when there is space in the row without necessity, this too is makruh. Evidence: (1) From Ibrahim: He disliked that he should pray in the 'taq' (arch/mihrab) of the imam. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). This effect indicates that an imam being in the mihrab is makruh. However, if the imam is outside the mihrab and performs sujud inside the mihrab, since there is no special feature for the imam in this case, it is permissible. (2) From Musa al-Juhani: The Messenger of Allah (saw) said: 'By Allah, this ummah (or 'my ummah') will remain upon good as long as they do not take in their mosques mihrabs like the mihrabs of the Christians.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). This effect indicates that it is not good to make mihrabs in mosques like the Christians. 'Madaih' means mihrab. (3) He was with Ammar bin Yasir in Madain... Hudhayfah said to him: 'Did you not hear the Messenger of Allah (saw) say: When a man leads people in prayer, he should not stand in a place higher than their place, or something similar?' Ammar said: 'That is why I followed you when you took hold of my hand.' (Abu Dawud, Mustadrak al-Hakim). This hadith indicates that the imam should not be on a higher place than the followers; similarly, if the imam is alone on a higher place, it is also makruh due to disrespect. (4) Complete the first row; for this there is this hadith: Anas narrated that the Messenger of Allah (saw) said: 'Complete the front row, then those that follow; whatever deficiency remains, let it be in the last row.' (Abu Dawud). These hadiths indicate that the first row should be filled. (5) Anas narrated: The Messenger of Allah (saw) said: 'Complete the rows, for I see you behind my back.' (Muslim).
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This ruling addresses disliked actions related to the imam's position in congregational prayer. The author states that it is makruh for the imam to stand alone in the mihrab (prayer niche) or on a raised platform, as this resembles the practice of Jews and Christians who elevate their leaders. Similarly, if a person stands alone behind the row when there is space in the row, it is also makruh because it disrupts congregation unity. The proofs include athar (companion statements) and hadith: Ibrahim al-Nakha'i disliked the imam praying in the 'taq' (arch); a hadith warns against adopting mihrabs like Christians; a hadith from Hudhayfah prohibits the imam standing higher than the congregation; and hadiths command completing the front rows. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the imam should be at the same level as the congregation, and rows should be completed without gaps.

Key Terms
محراب (mihrab): A niche in the mosque wall indicating the qiblah, often where the imam stands.
طاق (taq): An arch or niche; here synonymous with mihrab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it makruh for the imam to stand alone in the mihrab?
A) It distracts the congregation
B) It resembles the practice of Jews and Christians
C) It invalidates the prayer
D) It is prohibited by Quran

Key Takeaway
The imam should not stand alone in the mihrab or on a raised place; it is makruh tanzihi, and rows must be completed without gaps.

Ruling on Images During Prayer
States the ruling on images during prayer with exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on images during prayer and identify the three exceptions that remove the dislike.

Core Idea
Images of animate beings in prayer are makruh tanzih unless small, headless, or inanimate.

When praying, Muslims are encouraged to avoid anything that distracts or contradicts the spirit of devotion. The presence of images of living beings is one such concern. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: such images are disliked (makruh tanzih) but not prohibited, and three clear exceptions remove the dislike entirely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying with images of animate beings present. The ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked but valid).
The prayer remains valid even if disliked.
2
Recognize the three exceptions
The text mentions three cases where there is no harm: if the image is very small, if its head is cut off, or if it is of a non-living thing.
These exceptions remove the dislike completely.
3
Understand the rationale
The basis is hadith that angels do not enter houses with images; the exceptions are considered incomplete or insignificant.
Hanafis prioritize the general principle but allow exceptions based on need.
4
Apply to concrete scenarios
Determine whether a given image falls under the ruling or its exceptions by checking size, presence of head, and subject.
Use the three criteria as a checklist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۷۲ [ب]) ایسا کپڑا پہنا جس میں تصویر ہو، سر پر یا پیچھے یا سامنے یا مقابلہ میں تصویر ہونا، ہاں اگر بہت چھوٹی یا سرکٹی ہوئی یا غیر جاندار کی ہو تو حرج نہیں۔
Translation (572(b)): Wearing a garment in which there is a picture, or having a picture above his head, or behind him, or in front of him, or facing him, unless it is very small, or has its head cut off, or is of a non-living thing, then there is no harm.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This short ruling addresses the disliked nature of having images of living beings during prayer. The author states that it is makruh to wear clothing with pictures of animate objects, or to have such pictures above, behind, in front, or facing the worshipper. However, exceptions are made for images that are very small, have their heads cut off, or are of non-living things (like plants or inanimate objects). This is based on the established principle in Hanafi fiqh that images of living beings are prohibited or disliked, especially in places of worship, due to hadiths warning against angels entering houses with images. The exception for headless images is because the image is considered incomplete and thus not a true representation of a living being.

Key Terms
تصویر (taswir): An image or picture, especially of animate beings.
مقطوعة الرأس (maqtu'at al-ra's): An image with the head cut off, considered incomplete and thus not subject to the ruling.
مكروه تنزيهاً (makruh tanzihan): Disliked but not prohibited; the act is valid but better avoided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an exception to the ruling that images are makruh during prayer?
A) A large picture of a lion
B) A small picture of a bird with its head cut off
C) A picture of a tree
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Images of animate beings in prayer are makruh tanzih, but the dislike is removed if the image is very small, headless, or of an inanimate object.

Salah — Prayer

Disliked Acts in Prayer: Gaps, Images, and Fire
Lists disliked acts in prayer with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on praying in an imam's niche, standing behind gaps, and being near images or fire during prayer, and identify the hadith proofs for each.

Core Idea
Images in prayer are disliked unless small, headless, or inanimate; gaps in rows break congregation perfection.

The Hanafi school identifies several acts that are makruh during prayer, not by a single hadith but by a collection of evidence. These include the imam standing alone in a mihrab, wearing images, having animate images nearby, or facing fire or sleeping people. The rulings aim to preserve khushu and avoid resemblance to other faiths.

Guided Path
1
Identify each disliked act and its category
From the passage, list all actions declared makruh: praying alone in a niche, standing behind a gap, wearing images, having images around, and having fire or sleepers in front.
Each act has a separate hukm, but all are makruh.
2
Match each act to its proof
For each act, locate the specific hadith or athar cited. The imam's niche: athar from Ibrahim and hadith about Christian mihrabs. Gaps: hadiths on completing rows. Images: multiple hadiths (Aisha's cushion, Ibn Abbas on trees). Fire: implied by distraction.
Some acts rely on more than one proof.
3
Analyse wajh al-dalalah for images
Examine how the Prophet's reaction to the cushion with images yields makruh: he did not enter the house, showing disapproval. The Hanafi school interprets this as makruh tahrimi for large, complete images, but excludes small, defective, or inanimate images because the hadith says 'every image-maker in the Fire' but also allows trees.
The exception comes from the hadith 'if you must, make trees.'
4
Apply the Hanafi hierarchy of dislike
Determine whether these makruhat are tanzihi or tahrimi. For images, the threat of punishment suggests tahrimi. For other acts like standing alone in a mihrab, it is likely tanzihi unless they imitate disbelievers.
The text does not specify, but the strength of the dalil indicates tahrimi at least for large animate images.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Note that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may hold that any animate image in prayer is haram and invalidates prayer. The Hanafi position relies on the exceptions for small/headless/inanimate, which is a legitimate ikhtilaf in istinbat.
This difference stems from how the hadiths are reconciled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل ما يكره للمصلى وحده والقيام خلف صف فيه فرجة. (٥٧٢) ولبس ثوب فيه تصاوير وان يكون فوق رأسه او خلفه او بين يديه او بحذائه صورة الا ان تكون صغيرة او مقطوعة الرأس او لغير ذى روح. عن ابراهيم كان يكره أن يصلى في طاق الامام - (مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب صلوۃ الامام فی الطاق ، ج ثانی ص ٢٧٤، نمبر ٣٩١ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ٢٧٨ الصلوۃ فی الطاق ، ج اول ،ص ٤٠٩، نمبر ٤٦٩٧ ) عن موسى الجهني قال : قال رسول الله الا الله لا تزال هذه الامة أو قال أمتى بخير ما لم يتخذوا في مساجدهم مدائح كمدائح النصارى . (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ٢٧٨ الصلوة في الطاق، جاول، ص ٤٠٩، نمبر ٤٦٩٩) أنه كان مع عمار بن ياسر بالمدائن .... قال له حذيفة : ألم تسمع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : اذا أم الرجل القوم فلا يقم فى مكان أرفع من مقامهم . أو نحو ذالک قال عمار: لذالك اتبعتك حين أخذت على يدي . (ابوداود شریف ، باب الامام يقوم مكانا ارفع من مكان القوم ص ١٩٨ نمبر ٥٩٨ مستدرک للحاکم ، باب و من کتاب الامامۃ وصلاة الجماعة ، ج اول ،ص ٣٢٩، نمبر ٧٦٠ ) عن انس ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال أتموا الصف المقدم ثم الذين يليه فما كان من نقص فليكن في الصف الموخر . (ابوداود شریف، باب تسویۃ الصفوف ،ص ١٠٥، نمبر ٦٧) عن انس قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أتموا الصفوف فاني أراكم خلف ظهری (مسلم شریف، باب الصفوف تسوية الصفوف واقامتها، الخ، ص١٨٤، نمبر ٩٧٦/٤٣٤) عن عائشة أنها اشترت نمرقة فيها تصاوير فقام النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بالباب فلم يدخل فقلت أتوب الى الله مما أذنبت قال : ما هذه النمرقة ؟ قلت لتجلس عليها و توسدها قال ان أصحاب هذه الصورة يعذبون يوم القيامة - ( بخاری شریف، باب من كره القعود على الصورة ، ص ١٠٤٣، نمبر ٥٩٥٧ ر مسلم شریف، باب تحریم تصویر صورۃ الحیوان الخ۔ کتاب اللباس والزینۃ، ص ٩٤١ نمبر ٥٥٣١/٢١٠٧) عن عائشة قالت حشوت للنبى صلى الله عليه وسلم وسادة فيها تماثيل كانها نمرقة ، فجاء فقام بين الناس و جعل يتغير وجهه فقلت ما لنا يا رسول الله ؟ قال : ما بال هذه الوسادة؟ قلت وسادة جعلتها لك لتضطجع عليها قال أما علمت أن الملائكة لا تدخل بيتاً فيه صورة و ان من صنع الصورة يعذب يوم القيامة فيقول : أحيوا ما خلقتم ( بخارى شریف، باب اذا قال احد کم آمین و الملائكة في السماء فوافقت احدهما الاخرى غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه، ص ١٥٣٨، نمبر ٣٢٢٤ / مسلم شریف، باب تحریم تصویر صورۃ الحيوان الخ۔ کتاب اللباس والزینۃ ، ص ٩٤١ نمبر ٥٥٢٠/٢١٠٧) عن ابن عباس .... سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : كل مصور في النار يجعل له بكل صورة صورها ، نفساً فتعذبه في جهنم ، و قال ان كنت لا بد فاعلاً فاصنع الشجر و ما لا نفس له . فأقر به نصر بن علی (مسلم شریف، باب تحریم تصویر صورۃ الحیوان الخ ۔ کتاب اللباس والزینیۃ، ص ٩٤١، نمبر ٥٥٤٠/٢١١٠) وان يكون بين يديه تنور او كانون فيه جمر او قوم نيام (٥٧٣)
Chapter: What is disliked for the worshiper: [Praying] alone and standing behind a row in which there is a gap. (572) And wearing a garment on which there are images, and [if] there is an image above his head, or behind him, or in front of him, or opposite him, except if it is small, or its head is cut off, or it is of a non-sentient being. From Ibrahim: 'He disliked that one pray in the imam's niche' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq...). From Musa al-Juhani: 'He said: The Messenger of Allah (s) said: Indeed, this nation - or he said: my community - will continue in goodness as long as they do not take in their mosques mihrabs like the mihrabs of the Christians' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba...). 'That he was with Ammar ibn Yasir in al-Mada'in ... Hudhayfa said to him: Did you not hear the Messenger of Allah (s) say: When a man leads the people, he should not stand in a place higher than their station?' (Abu Dawud...). From Anas: 'The Messenger of Allah (s) said: Complete the front row, then the one next to it, and whatever deficiency remains, let it be in the last row' (Abu Dawud...). From Anas: 'The Messenger of Allah (s) said: Complete the rows, for I see you behind my back' (Muslim...). From Aisha: 'She bought a cushion with images, then the Prophet (s) stood at the door and did not enter... He said: The owners of these images will be tormented on the Day of Resurrection' (Bukhari, Muslim...). From Aisha: 'I padded a pillow for the Prophet (s) with figures... He said: Do you not know that the angels do not enter a house in which there is an image, and the maker of the image will be tormented on the Day of Resurrection?' (Bukhari, Muslim...). From Ibn Abbas: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah (s) say: Every image-maker is in the Fire... If you must do it, then make trees and what has no soul' (Muslim...). And [it is disliked] that in front of him there be an oven or a stove with embers, or sleeping people. (573)
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings with proofs concerning disliked acts (makruhat) during prayer. The author first states the ruling: it is disliked for the imam to pray alone in a niche (mihrab) or in an elevated place, or for a worshiper to stand behind a row that has a gap. This is disliked because it resembles the practice of Jews and Christians; the imam should not separate himself or appear above the congregation. Proofs include the effect of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i disliking praying in the imam's niche, and hadiths warning against taking mihrabs like Christians, standing higher than the congregation, and completing first rows. The second group of rulings concerns images: wearing clothes with images or having an image above, behind, in front, or beside the worshiper is disliked, except if the image is very small, its head is cut off, or it is of a non-sentient being (trees, etc.). This is proven by hadiths where the Prophet disapproved of cushions with images and stated that angels do not enter a house with an image, and that image-makers will be punished. The Hanafi position is that such images are disliked but not forbidden when used in contexts of lowliness (like underfoot) or if they are small. Finally, having an oven or stove with fire in front of the worshiper, or sleeping people, is disliked because it may cause distraction or resemble fire-worshippers. All these rulings aim to protect the concentration (khushu') in prayer.

Key Terms
طاق الامام (taq al-imam): The niche (mihrab) where the imam stands alone.
مدائح (mada'ih): Mihrabs, niche-like structures in mosques.
نمرقة (numruqah): A small cushion or rug used for sitting.
تنور (tannur): An oven or stove for baking.
كانون (kanun): A stove or brazier for fire.
ذو روح (dhu ruh): A living being, an animate creature.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person prays while wearing a garment on which there is a small image of a bird?
A) The prayer is invalid (batil).
B) It is disliked (makruh).
C) It is permissible and not disliked.
D) It is forbidden (haram).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school specifies that while certain acts are makruh in prayer, they do not invalidate it; the most significant is the presence of large animate images, which is prohibitively disliked.

Disliked Acts in Prayer: Images, Fire, and Sleeping People
Rulings on disliked acts in prayer with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi rulings regarding images, fire, and sleeping persons during prayer and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Praying with animate images or in front of fire/sleeping people is makruh tanzih due to distraction and resemblance to non-Islamic practices.

The Hanafi school provides clear guidance on acts that are disliked during prayer. This lesson covers two specific situations: having images of living beings on clothing or nearby, and praying in front of a fire or sleeping people. We will explore the rulings and their proofs from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Determine the specific acts being discussed: praying while wearing or facing an animate image, and praying in front of a fire (tannur or kanun) or behind sleeping people. The ruling for both is makruh tanzih (slightly disliked).
Makruh tanzih means it is better to avoid, but the prayer remains valid.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
For images, the proofs are hadiths from Aisha: the Prophet refused to enter her room when she had a cushion with images, and he said angels do not enter a house with images. For fire and sleeping people, the proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Do not pray behind a sleeping person or one who speaks.'
These are ahad hadith, thus zanni al-thubut, supporting a ruling of karahah, not tahrim.
3
Understand the rationale (illah)
Images are disliked because they distract and resemble idols; fire is disliked because it mimics fire-worshippers and poses a distraction; sleeping people may break wind or mumble, disturbing khushu'.
The illah for fire also includes the risk of burning and distraction.
4
Note the exceptions and contextual applications
Images are not disliked if placed under the feet, very small, headless, or of inanimate objects. In villages, lighting candles for light is permissible because it is not for worship. Sleeping people are disliked only if they are many and likely to cause disturbance.
The exception for candles shows that the ruling is contextual (urf and necessity).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل ما يكره للمصلى
(۵۷۳) وان يكون بين يديه تنور او کانون فيه جمر او قوم نيام تشریح : ایسا کپڑا پہن کر نماز پڑھنا جس میں تصویر ہو مکروہ ہے۔ یا ایسی جگہ تصویر ہو جس سے اس کی تعظیم معلوم ہو تو یہ بھی مکر وہ ہے، مثلا سر پر یا سامنے یا مقابلے میں تصویر ہو تو مکروہ ہے، البتہ تصویر پاؤں کے نیچے ہو اس کی تو ہین ہے اس لئے مکروہ نہیں ، بہت چھوٹی تصویر جو نظر نہ آتی ہو، یا تصویر کا سر کٹا ہوا ہو، یا غیر جاندار کی تصویر ہو تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔

صلى الله
ترجمه : (۵۷۳) سامنے تنور یا آتشدان آگ والا ہو یا سوئے ہوئے لوگ ہوں تشریح : سامنے چولھا ہو یا آتشداں [ بہاری میں ۔ بورسی] ہو اور اس میں آگ ہو تو نماز مکروہ ہے،اس کی ایک وجہ یہ ہے کہ پارسی لوگ آگ کی عبادت کرتے ہیں تو لوگ ایسانہ سمجھے کہ آگ کی پوجا کر رہا ہے، دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ آگ سے جلنے کا خطرہ ہوگا اس لئے خشوع خضوع باقی نہیں رہے گا اس لئے بھی مکروہ ہے۔ اور بہت سے سوئے ہوئے لوگ ہوں تو ہوسکتا ہے کہ وہ حدث کرے یا بڑ بڑائے جس سے نماز میں خلل ہو اس لئے مکروہ ہے۔ دیہات میں روشنی کے لئے موم بتی جلا کر صف کے سامنے رکھتے ہیں، اس
کی گنجائش ہے، کیونکہ وہ پوجا کے لئے نہیں رکھتے ، اور روشنی کرنے کی مجبوری ہے۔
صل الله
وجه : (ا) عبد الله بن عباس أن النبي علم قال : لا تصلوا خلف النائم و لا المتحدث ۔(ابوداود شریف باب الصلوة الى المتحدثين والنيام ،ص ۱۰۸، نمبر ۶۹۴ رابن ماجه ، باب من صلی و بینه و بین القبلہ شی ء ص ۱۳۵، نمبر ۹۵۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سونے والے کے پیچھے نماز نہ پڑھے۔
لغت : تنور : چولھا۔ کانون آتشدان ۔ جمر: چنگاری۔
Chapter on what is disliked for the one praying. (573) And that there be in front of him a tandoor or a brazier with embers, or sleeping people. Explanation: Praying wearing a cloth that has an image is disliked. Or if there is an image in a place from which its veneration is known (e.g., on the head or in front or opposite), that is also disliked. However, if the image is under the feet, that is considered disrespectful, so it is not disliked. A very small image that is not visible, or the head of the image is cut off, or an image of an inanimate object, then there is no harm. Proof: (1) In this hadith... (2) ... (3) ... Translation: (573) In front of a tandoor or a brazier with fire, or sleeping people. Explanation: If there is a stove or brazier with fire in front, then prayer is disliked... And if there are many sleeping people, it is disliked... In villages, they light candles for light in front of the row, that is permissible. Proof: (a) Hadith of Abdullah ibn Abbas: Do not pray behind a sleeping person or one who is speaking. Vocabulary: Tandoor: oven. Canon: brazier. Jamr: ember.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct disliked actions in prayer under one heading (573). The first ruling concerns images (taswir): it is makruh to pray while wearing a garment with images of animate beings, or to have such images in front of oneself or in a place of veneration. However, if the image is under the feet, is very small, has its head cut off, or is of an inanimate object (e.g., trees), it is not disliked. The proof is from multiple hadith: the Prophet disliked sitting on a cushion with images, and angels do not enter a house with an image. The second ruling concerns praying in front of a fire (in a tandoor or brazier) or near sleeping people. It is makruh because it resembles fire-worshippers (Zoroastrians) and because it disturbs khushu' (humility), or because sleeping people may break wind or mumble, disturbing the prayer. The proof is a hadith: 'Do not pray behind a sleeping person or one who speaks.'

Key Terms
تصویر (taswir): Image of an animate being (human or animal) on clothing or other objects.
تنور (tannur): An oven or tandoor used for baking; here meaning a source of fire in front of the worshipper.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; an action that should be avoided but is not sinful. In Hanafi fiqh, it is a category between halal and haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, which of the following is NOT considered makruh in prayer?
A) Praying while wearing a shirt with a small image of a bird on the sleeve that is easily visible.
B) Praying in front of a tandoor that has glowing embers.
C) Praying on a mat that has a large picture of a mountain.
D) Praying behind a group of sleeping people.

Key Takeaway
Animate images in venerated positions and praying in front of fire or sleeping people are makruh tanzih in Hanafi fiqh, with clear exceptions and context-based relaxations.

Wiping Dust from the Forehead During Prayer
Ruling on wiping dust in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping dust from the forehead during prayer and explain why it is disliked using the provided hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Non-harmful dust on the forehead should be left until after prayer; wiping it is makruh.

During prayer, small amounts of dust may settle on the forehead from prostration. Should one wipe it off immediately or leave it? The Hanafi school addresses this with a clear ruling based on prophetic practice and companion statements. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind the disliked nature of this action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping non-harmful dust from the forehead during prayer. Determine its hukm: the text states it is makruh (disliked).
Makruh tanzih means better to avoid but prayer remains valid.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites two proofs: (1) The Prophet's practice of leaving mud on his forehead while prostrating, and (2) Ibn Abbas's explicit prohibition of wiping until after prayer.
The hadith from Bukhari shows the Prophet did not wipe, indicating it is not required.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's omission of wiping shows that wiping is not part of the prayer's perfection; Ibn Abbas's command to delay wiping until after prayer implies it is disliked during.
Wiping constitutes an unnecessary minor action (amal qalil), which is discouraged.
4
Note the exception
If the dust is harmful (e.g., causes irritation), then wiping becomes permissible.
The ruling specifically applies to 'non-harmful' dust.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۷۴) نماز میں پیشانی سے غیر مضر مٹی صاف کرنا۔
تشریح جو مٹی نقصان نہ دیتی ہو اس کو نماز کے درمیان پیشانی سے جھاڑ نا مکروہ ہے، کیونکہ اس سے عمل قلیل ہونے کا خطرہ ہے وجه : (ا)سـألـت ابا سعيد الخدري فقال رأيت رسول الله الله يسجد في الماء و الطين حتى رأيت اثر الطين في جبهته ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب من لم یج جھتہ وانفه حتی صلی ص ۱۳۶، نمبر ۸۳۶)(۲) عن ابن عباس انه قال لا يمسح وجهه من التراب في الصلاة حتى يتشهد و يسلم - (سنن بیہقی ، باب لا يمسح وجمعه من التراب في الصلاة حتى یسلم ، ج ثانی ص ۴۰۶ نمبر ۳۵۵۳)
Translation: (574) Wiping non-harmful dust from the forehead in prayer. Explanation: Dust that is not harmful, wiping it from the forehead during prayer is disliked, because there is a risk of it being a small action (amal qalil). Proof: (1) I asked Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and he said: I saw the Messenger of Allah prostrating in water and mud until I saw the effect of mud on his forehead. (Bukhari) (2) Ibn Abbas said: He should not wipe his face from dust in prayer until he finishes tashahhud and gives salams. (Bayhaqi)
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This ruling concerns a small, non-harmful amount of dust on the forehead during prayer. The Hanafi position is that it is makruh to wipe it away while the prayer is ongoing, because it constitutes an unnecessary action (amal qalil) that may disturb the prayer's solemnity. The proof is from the practice of the Prophet: he did not wipe the mud from his forehead when prostrating on muddy ground, indicating that leaving it is better. Additionally, the saying of Ibn Abbas explicitly prohibits wiping the face from dust until after the prayer is complete.

Key Terms
عمل قلیل (amal qalil): A minor action that does not invalidate the prayer but is discouraged.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; better to avoid but prayer remains valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this lesson, why is it disliked to wipe non-harmful dust from the forehead during prayer?
A) Because it invalidates the prayer
B) Because it involves an unnecessary minor action
C) Because dust is impure
D) Because it resembles the practice of non-Muslims

Key Takeaway
Wiping non-harmful dust from the forehead during prayer is makruh tanzih; leave it until after prayer to avoid unnecessary minor actions.

Disliked: Designating a Specific Surah Exclusively
Ruling on designating a specific surah exclusively

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on designating a specific surah for exclusive recitation in prayer and identify the two exceptions that remove the dislike.

Core Idea
Restricting prayer recitation to a single surah is makruh tanzih unless done for ease or to seek blessing from the Prophet's practice.

This lesson addresses a common practice: reciting only one surah repeatedly in prayer. While the Hanafi school generally dislikes this, it recognizes valid reasons such as physical ease or following the Sunnah. Understanding the nuance prevents unnecessary rigidity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the practice of restricting oneself to reciting only one specific surah in prayer, to the exclusion of all others.
2
State the General Ruling
The Hanafi ruling: this practice is makruh tanzih (disliked, not sinful). The dislike is due to implying neglect of other surahs.
3
Identify the Exceptions
There are two exceptions: (1) reciting a surah the Prophet recited for tabarruk (seeking blessing), and (2) reciting a surah because it is easier for the person (e.g., due to old age or difficulty). In these cases, the dislike is removed.
4
Understand the Rationale
The ruling is based on the intention: if the intention is to disregard other surahs, it is disliked. If the intention is ease or blessing, there is no disregard, so it is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۷۵) کسی سورت کا اس طرح مقرر کر لینا کہ اس کے سوا دوسری نہ پڑھے ،مگر ہاں آسانی کے لئے یا رسول اللہ ے کی پڑھی ہوئی سورت کو برکت کے لئے پڑھے تو مکروہ نہیں۔ تشریح : کسی سورت کو خاص کر کے بار بار پڑھے تو اس کی اہمیت ہوگی ، اور اس کے برخلاف دوسری سورتوں سے بے اعتنائی ہوگی اس لئے کسی سورت کو خاص کرنا مکروہ ہے ، ہاں اگر کسی سورت کو حضور نے پڑھی ہے اس لئے برکت کے لئے اس کو پڑھے، یاوہ
اس کے لئے آسان ہے اس لئے وہ پڑھ رہا ہے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے، کیونکہ اس میں بے اعتنائی نہیں ہے۔
Translation: (575) Designating a surah so that he recites nothing else, unless for ease or for seeking blessing from the recitation of the Prophet (may peace be upon him), then it is not disliked. Explanation: If a person specifically recites a particular surah repeatedly, it will give it importance and show disregard for other surahs, so it is disliked. However, if he recites a surah that the Prophet recited for seeking blessing, or because it is easier for him, then there is no harm, because there is no disregard.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This ruling addresses the practice of restricting oneself to reciting only one surah in prayer, to the exclusion of all others. The Hanafi position is that this is generally makruh because it may imply a preference or neglect of other surahs. However, there are two exceptions: (1) if the person recites a surah that the Prophet (peace be upon him) specifically recited, seeking barakah (blessing); or (2) if he recites a surah because it is easier for him (due to weakness or difficulty memorizing others). In these cases, it is not disliked because the intention is not to disregard other surahs.

Key Terms
تعیین سورة (ta'yin surah): Designating a specific surah for exclusive recitation in prayer.
تبرک (tabarruk): Seeking blessing (barakah) by following the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Reciting because the Prophet recited it for blessing.
B) Reciting because it is easier due to old age.
C) Reciting because you like the surah more.
D) Reciting because it is the only surah you have memorized and you cannot memorize more.

Key Takeaway
Designating a specific surah exclusively in prayer is makruh tanzih unless done for ease or tabarruk.

Sutrah in Salah: When Is Its Omission Disliked?
Ruling on sutrah: when to use, when omission is disliked.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using a sutrah and explain when omitting it is disliked, using the hadith of Abu Dhar as proof.

Core Idea
Omitting a sutrah is disliked when passersby are expected; its purpose is to protect khushu' and prevent sin.

This passage addresses the importance of using a sutrah (screen) when praying in an open area where people may pass. The Hanafi school teaches that while sutrah is not obligatory, neglecting it in such a situation is makruh tanzih. The proof is from the hadith of Abu Dhar, which instructs the worshipper to have something screening him. Understanding this ruling helps maintain the quality of prayer and avoid discouraging others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is omitting a sutrah in a place where passersby are expected. The Hanafi ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked, but not sinful).
Makruh tanzih means it is better to avoid, but the prayer remains valid.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Abu Dhar: 'When one of you stands for prayer, he should have something screening him...' Although the text is incomplete, it is a well-known hadith.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain), giving zanni (speculative) certainty.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form ('should have') indicates a recommendation, not an obligation. The context of passersby triggers the dislike when omitted.
The command is understood as sunnah, not fard.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools consider sutrah wajib (obligatory) in certain situations, such as in a mosque or where people pass.
The Hanafi school relies on other evidence that permits praying without a sutrah in private.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that sutrah is recommended; omitting it is only disliked if passersby are expected. This balances the hadith with general permissibility.
The ruling is practical: it protects khushu' without imposing undue hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۷۶) مصلی کے سامنے سے جہاں لوگوں کے گذرنے کا گمان ہوسترہ نہ رکھنا مکروہ ہے۔ تشریح : آدمی میدان میں نماز پڑھ رہا ہو اور خطرہ ہو کہ اس کے سامنے سے آدمی گزرے گا تو اس کو چاہئے کہ سترہ بنالے، اور سترہ کی سہولت نہ ہو تو سامنے خط بھینچ دے تا کہ گزرنے والا گنہ گار نہ ہو اور نماز کے خشوع و خضوع میں خلل انداز نہ ہو۔ ہاں جہاں آدمی کے گزرنے کا خطرہ نہ ہو وہاں سترہ نہ بنائے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابی ذر قال قال رسول الله الله الله اذا قام احدكم يصلى فانه يستره اذا كان بين
Translation: (576) Not taking a sutrah in a place where one suspects people will pass in front of the worshipper is disliked. Explanation: If a person is praying in an open area and there is a risk that someone will pass in front of him, he should take a sutrah (screen), and if he cannot easily get a sutrah, he should draw a line in front of him, so that the passer-by is not sinful and the khushu' of prayer is not disturbed. However, if there is no risk of anyone passing, then there is no harm if he does not take a sutrah. Proof: (1) The hadith from Abu Dhar: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When one of you stands for prayer, he should have something screening him if there is (something in front of him)...'
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This ruling concerns the sutrah (a screen or object placed in front of the worshipper) in prayer. The Hanafi position is that it is makruh to omit the sutrah if there is a reasonable expectation that people may pass in front of the worshipper. The purpose is to prevent passersby from committing a sin (by crossing in front of someone praying) and to maintain khushu' (humility). If a physical sutrah is not available, drawing a line is sufficient. The ruling is based on the hadith of Abu Dhar (partially quoted, but known from other sources) which instructs the worshipper to place something in front of him. If no passersby are expected, it is not disliked to pray without a sutrah.

Key Terms
سترة (sutrah): A screen, wall, stick, or line placed in front of the worshipper to prevent people from passing directly in front.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it disliked (makruh) to pray without a sutrah according to this passage?
A) When praying at home alone
B) When praying in a mosque with no one passing
C) When praying in an open field where people may pass
D) When the sutrah is not available at all

Key Takeaway
Omitting a sutrah when passersby are expected is makruh tanzih; using it preserves khushu' and prevents sin.

Ruling on Specifying a Particular Surah in Prayer
Ruling on always reciting a specific surah to the exclusion of others

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on specifying a particular surah in prayer and identify the exceptions when it is not disliked.

Core Idea
Specifying a single surah repeatedly is makruh unless done for ease or to follow the Prophet's practice.

This lesson addresses a common practice: always reciting the same surah in prayer. While it may seem like devotion, the Hanafi school warns that it can lead to neglect of other parts of the Quran. However, the ruling is nuanced—certain intentions, such as seeking barakah from the Prophet's recitation or choosing an easier surah, remove the dislike. We will examine the reasoning behind this ruling and learn to apply it correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The act is 'ta'yīn sūra'—specifying a particular surah to the exclusion of all others in prayer. The default Hanafi ruling is that it is makruh (disliked).
Makruh here means makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked), not sinful but better avoided.
2
Understand the reason for dislike
The reason is that consistently reciting one surah implies preference for it over others, leading to neglect of other Quranic verses. This contradicts the spirit of reciting diverse portions of the Quran.
The principle at play is avoiding excessive specialization that causes disregard for other parts of revelation.
3
Identify the exceptions
Two exceptions lift the dislike: (1) reciting a surah because the Prophet (ﷺ) often recited it, seeking barakah; (2) reciting a surah because it is easier for the person (e.g., shorter or better memorized).
In both cases, there is no disregard for other surahs; the intent is following Sunnah or facilitating worship.
4
Apply the ruling to scenarios
Test different scenarios: if a person always recites Surah al-Ikhlas because they love it, it is makruh. If they recite it because the Prophet (ﷺ) often recited it (e.g., in witr), it is not makruh.
The distinction hinges on intention (niyyah) and the presence or absence of neglect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٥٧٥) وتعيين سورة لا يقرأ غيرها الا ليسر عليه وتبركا بقراءة النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم. تشريح: کسی سورت کو خاص کر کے بار بار پڑھے تو اس کی اہمیت ہوگی، اور اس کے برخلاف دوسری سورتوں سے بے اعتنائی ہوگی اس لئے کسی سورت کو خاص کرنا مکروہ ہے، ہاں اگر کسی سورت کو حضور نے پڑھی ہے اس لئے برکت کے لئے اس کو پڑھے، یا وہ اس کے لئے آسان ہے اس لئے وہ پڑھ رہا ہے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے، کیونکہ اس میں بے اعتنائی نہیں ہے۔
(575) And specifying a surah that he does not read other than it, except for ease upon him and as a blessing by reading what the Prophet (ﷺ) recited. Explanation: If he repeatedly recites a particular surah, it will give it significance, and in contrast, there will be disregard for other surahs. Therefore, specifying a particular surah is disliked. However, if he recites a surah because the Prophet (ﷺ) recited it for blessing, or because it is easy for him, then there is no harm, because there is no disregard in that.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This ruling deals with the practice of always reciting the same surah in prayer. The author explains that this is makruh (disliked) because it shows preference for one surah over others, potentially leading to neglect of other parts of the Quran. However, two exceptions are noted: if one recites a surah that the Prophet (ﷺ) frequently recited for the sake of barakah (blessing), or if the surah is easier for the person due to memorization or difficulty, then it is not disliked. The author does not cite specific textual evidence here, but the ruling is based on the principle of avoiding innovation and maintaining balance.

Key Terms
تعيين سورة (ta'yīn sūra): Specifying a particular surah to be recited exclusively in prayer
تبرك (tabarruk): Seeking blessing by following the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which case is it NOT disliked to specify a particular surah in prayer?
A) When one wants to memorize the surah
B) When one recites it for ease or barakah
C) When it is shorter than other surahs
D) When one is leading the prayer

Key Takeaway
Specifying a particular surah in prayer is makruh unless it is for ease or to seek blessing from the Prophet's practice.

Ruling on Not Using a Sutrah When People May Pass
Dislike of praying without a sutrah when passersby are expected

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using a sutrah in prayer and apply it to different scenarios based on the likelihood of passersby.

Core Idea
A sutrah is recommended when passersby are expected; omitting it when necessary is makruh tanzih, not sinful when none are expected.

The prayer is a protected space, both physically and spiritually. The sutrah serves as a barrier to prevent the sin of a passerby and to safeguard the worshiper's concentration. This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on when a sutrah is recommended and when it is not needed, based on the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon: leaving the sutrah when people may pass. The ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked).
The dislike is due to potential disruption of prayer and causing sin to the passerby.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the hadith of Abu Dharr in Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud, which emphasizes the need for a sutrah.
The hadith mentions that a donkey, woman, and black dog can break the prayer if they pass without a sutrah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith implies that having a sutrah prevents prayer breakage; conversely, not having one when needed is blameworthy.
The command 'fainnahu yasturuhu' indicates recommendation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may consider sutrah as sunnah mu'akkadah in all circumstances, but the Hanafi position is context-dependent.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different interpretations of the hadith.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that it is recommended (or at least not sinful) to omit sutrah when no one is expected; otherwise it is makruh tanzih.
The authority is zahir al-riwayah from the core Hanafi texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٥٧٦) و ترک اتخاذ سترة في محل يظنّ مروره. تشريح: آدمي میدان میں نماز پڑھ رہا ہو اور خطرہ ہو کہ اس کے سامنے سے آدمی گزرے گا تو اس کو چاہئے کہ سترہ بنا لے، اور سترہ کی سہولت نہ ہو تو سامنے خط کھینچ دے تا کہ گزرنے والا گنہگار نہ ہو اور نماز کے خشوع و خضوع میں خلل انداز نہ ہو۔ ہاں جہاں آدمی کے گزرنے کا خطرہ نہ ہو وہاں سترہ نہ بنائے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ وجه: (۱) حديث ہے عن ابي ذر قال قال رسول الله ﷺ اذا قام احدكم يصلى فانه يستره اذا كان بين يدي مثل آخرة الرحل، فاذا لم يكن بين يديه مثل آخرة الرحل فانه يقطع صلاته الحمار، و المرأة و الكلب الاسود (مسلم شریف، باب قدر ما يستر المصلي، ص ۲۰۹ نمبر ۱۱۳۷/۵۱۰ ابوداود شریف، باب ما يستر المصلي، ص ۱۰۸، نمبر ۶۸۵). اس حديث میں ہے کہ کجاوے کی طرح کوئی چیز سامنے ہو تو وہ سترہ بن جائے گا۔
(576) And leaving the taking of a sutrah in a place where passing is suspected. Explanation: If a person is praying in an open field and there is fear that someone might pass in front of him, he should take a sutrah. If taking a sutrah is not easy, he should draw a line in front so that the passerby does not sin and so that his humility in prayer is not disturbed. However, in a place where there is no risk of someone passing, there is no harm if he does not take a sutrah. Evidence: (1) Hadith from Abu Dharr who said: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: When one of you stands to pray, he should take a sutrah if there is something like the back of a camel saddle in front of him. If there is nothing like the back of a camel saddle in front of him, then a donkey, a woman, and a black dog nullify his prayer. (Muslim, chapter on the measure of what screens the worshiper, p. 209, no. 1137/510; Abu Dawud, chapter on what screens the worshiper, p. 108, no. 685). This hadith indicates that if something like a saddle is in front, it serves as a sutrah.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This ruling states that it is makruh (disliked) to pray without a sutrah when there is a likelihood of people passing in front. The author explains that the purpose of the sutrah is to prevent the sin of the passerby and to protect the worshiper's concentration. If a physical sutrah is not available, drawing a line on the ground suffices. However, if there is no risk of anyone passing, there is no obligation to use a sutrah. The evidence is from the hadith of Abu Dharr which stresses the importance of having something in front, and warns that certain things (donkey, woman, black dog) can invalidate prayer if they pass directly in front without a sutrah.

Key Terms
سترة (sutrah): An object placed in front of the person praying to prevent anyone passing directly in front
آخرة الرحل (ākhirat al-rahil): The back part of a camel saddle, used as a benchmark for minimum height of a sutrah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person prays in a place where no one is expected to pass, what is the ruling on not using a sutrah?
A) Makruh (disliked)
B) Haram (forbidden)
C) No harm (no sin)
D) Wajib (obligatory)

Key Takeaway
A sutrah is recommended when passersby are expected; omitting it then is makruh tanzih, but not sinful when no one is likely to pass.

Recommended Sutrah Dimensions: One Arm High, One Finger Thick
Ruling on recommended sutrah dimensions with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the recommended dimensions of the sutrah and cite the primary textual evidence (hadith and athar) that supports it.

Core Idea
The sutrah should be at least one arm in height and one finger in thickness to prevent passing.

When praying in an open space where passersby may cross, the Hanafi school recommends planting a sutrah (screen) that is visible from a distance. This ruling preserves the worshipper's concentration (khushu) and is based on the Prophet's example. In this lesson, we explore the physical specifications of the sutrah and the evidence that defines them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage rules upon: the act of planting a sutrah when one expects people to pass. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.
The text uses 'yastahibbu lahu' (it is preferred) which indicates mustahabb.
2
Locate the specific dimensions
Extract the two dimensions: height of one arm (dhira') and thickness of one finger (ghilz al-isba'). Note that 'or more' allows flexibility.
A dhira' is approximately 45-50 cm; a finger's thickness is about 2 cm.
3
Analyze the first evidence – hadith
Relate the hadith of Abu Dharr wherein the Prophet compared the sutrah to the back of a camel saddle. This indicates a height of about one arm, as the saddle's back is that high.
The hadith also describes what breaks the prayer if no sutrah is present, but here the focus is on its size.
4
Analyze the second evidence – athar
The practice of Ibn Umar is cited: he would only pray towards a sutrah of one arm height. This confirms the measurement from a Companion.
This athar strengthens the hadith evidence.
5
Understand the rationale
The dimensions ensure visibility from a distance, so a person will walk around the sutrah rather than cross in front of the praying person.
The objective is to protect khushu, not merely to fulfill a formality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٥٧٧) اذا ظنّ مروره يستحب له ان يغرز سترة تكون طول ذراع فصاعدا في غلظ الاصبع. تشريح: نمازی آدمی کے سامنے سے کوئی گزرے گا تو اس کا خشوع و خضوع ختم ہو جائے گا اس لئے اگر میدان میں نماز پڑھ رہا ہو اور کسی کے گزرنے کا خطرہ ہو تو سامنے سترہ گاڑ دے، جو دور سے نظر آسکے، اور اس کا اندازہ یہ ہے کہ ایک ہاتھ یا اس سے زیادہ لمبا ہو اور ایک انگلی کی مقدار چوڑا ہو۔ وجه: (۱) ایک ہاتھ اونچا سترہ ہوگا تو دور سے آدمی کو نظر آئے گا تو نمازی اس سے دور ہو کر چلے گا، اور اسکے سامنے سے نہیں گزرے گا۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کجاوے کی مانند سترہ اونچا ہو۔ عن ابي ذر قال قال رسول الله ﷺ اذا قام احدكم يصلى فانه يستره اذا كان بين يديه مثل آخرة الرحل، فاذا لم يكن بين يديه مثل آخرة الرحل فانه يقطع صلاته الحمار، و المرأة و الكلب الاسود (مسلم شریف، باب قدر ما يستر المصلي، ص ۲۰۹، نمبر ۱۱۳۷/۵۱۰، ابو داود شریف، باب ما يستر المصلي، ص ۱۰۸، نمبر ۶۸۵). اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کجاوے کی طرح کوئی چیز سامنے ہو تو وہ سترہ بن جائے گا۔ اور یہ تقریباً ایک ہاتھ اونچا ہوتا ہے، اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک ہاتھ اونچا ہو۔ (۳) اس اثر میں اسکا ثبوت ہے۔ كان ابن عمر لا يصلى الا الى السترة قال : كان قدر مؤخرة رحله، ذراع. (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب قدر ما يستر المصلي، ج ثانی، ص ۳ نمبر ۲۲۷۷). اس اثر میں ہے کہ حضرت ابن عمر کا سترہ ایک ہاتھ لمبا ہوتا تھا۔ (۴) سترہ ایک انگلی کے برابر موٹا ہو۔
(577) When he suspects passing, it is mustahabb for him to plant a sutrah whose length is an arm or more, and whose thickness is a finger. Explanation: If someone passes in front of the person praying, his humility and concentration will be destroyed. Therefore, if he is praying in an open field and there is risk of someone passing, he should plant a sutrah in front that is visible from a distance. Its measure is that it should be an arm or more in height and a finger's width in thickness. Evidence: (1) A sutrah of one arm height will be visible from a distance, so a person will go around it and not pass directly in front. (2) In the hadith, it is mentioned that a sutrah should be like the back of a camel saddle. From Abu Dharr: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: When one of you stands to pray, he should take a sutrah if there is something like the back of a camel saddle in front of him. If there is nothing like the back of a camel saddle in front of him, then a donkey, a woman, and a black dog nullify his prayer. (Muslim, chapter on the measure of what screens the worshiper, p. 209, no. 1137/510; Abu Dawud, chapter on what screens the worshiper, p. 108, no. 685). This indicates that something like a camel saddle serves as a sutrah, and that is approximately one arm in height. (3) This is also confirmed in the athar: Ibn Umar would not pray except towards a sutrah, and he said: It was the size of the back of his saddle, one arm. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on the measure of what screens the worshiper, vol. 2, p. 3, no. 2277). (4) The sutrah should be a finger in thickness.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This ruling provides the recommended specifications for the sutrah when one expects passersby. The height should be at least one forearm (dhira') and the thickness about the width of a finger. The author explains that this ensures the sutrah is visible from a distance so people will avoid passing directly in front. The evidence comes from the hadith of Abu Dharr which compares the sutrah to the back of a camel saddle, which is approximately one arm in height. Additionally, the practice of Ibn Umar confirms this measurement. The thickness is derived from the general principle that the sutrah should be substantial enough to serve its purpose.

Key Terms
ذراع (dhira'): A unit of length measured from the elbow to the fingertips, approximately 45-50 cm
غلظ الاصبع (ghilz al-isba'): Thickness of a finger, approximately 2 cm

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the sutrah being one arm in height?
A) The Quranic verse on prayer barriers
B) The hadith comparing it to the back of a camel saddle
C) The consensus of the Companions
D) The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa alone

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends a sutrah of at least one arm in height and one finger in thickness, based on the prophetic example and the practice of Ibn Umar.

Recommended Dimensions of the Sutrah in Salah
Ruling on the recommended dimensions of the sutrah for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sutrah, specify its recommended dimensions, and cite the primary proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
A sutrah of one cubit high and finger thick is recommended to protect prayer from interruption.

When praying in an open space, passers-by can disrupt one's focus. The Hanafi school teaches that placing a sutrah (barrier) in front of you is a recommended practice, not an obligation. The dimensions given—one cubit in height and finger thickness—are based on prophetic guidance. This lesson unpacks the proof and reasoning behind these dimensions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text discusses the sutrah—an object placed in front of the praying person. Determine whether the Hanafi school considers it obligatory, recommended, or merely permissible. Look for the term 'yastaḥibbu' (يستحب) in the translation.
The ruling is mustahabb (recommended).
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith of Abu Dharr in the source. It states that if there is no sutrah like the back of a camel saddle, the prayer is cut off by certain things. This hadith is the main evidence for the height of the sutrah.
The hadith is from Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'مثل آخرة الرحل' (like the back of the camel saddle) indicates a height of approximately one cubit. The text reasons that a sutrah of this height is visible from a distance, so people will walk around it. This shows how the proof yields the ruling.
The comparison is analogical, not literal.
4
Note the additional evidence
The athar from Ibn Umar shows that his sutrah was one cubit long. This supports the recommended dimension from the practice of a Companion.
The athar is from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
5
Recognize the ikhtilaf
Unlike the Hanafi school, the Shafi'i school considers the sutrah obligatory (wajib) for those praying outside a masjid. Identify the practical difference this makes in fiqh.
This is an inter-madhhab dispute.

Source Text
