Chapter on what is not disliked for the one praying. (584) It is not disliked for him to tie his waist nor to hang a sword or similar item when he is not occupied by its movement. (585) And inserting his hands into the open front or back of a qaba (open-front garment), according to the chosen position, is not disliked. (586) And facing a Mushaf, a hanging sword, the back of a sitting person conversing, or a candle or lamp is not disliked according to the correct view. (587) And prostrating on a rug containing pictures while not prostrating on the pictures is not disliked.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage is a section ruling on actions that are not disliked (makruh) during prayer. It opens the chapter 'Things Not Disliked for the One Praying'. The author lists several actions and explains why they are not makruh, often with evidence.

First Ruling (584): It is not disliked to fasten a belt or waistband, or to wear a sword or similar item, provided the worshipper is not distracted by their movement. The commentary mentions that pilgrims often carry money belts, and warriors wear swords, so these are permissible. The evidence given is the practice of a Muhrim (one in ihram) wearing a belt, which shows its basic permissibility.

Second Ruling (585): It is not disliked to insert one's hands into a qaba (a garment open at the front and back) if the awrah is not exposed and concentration is not disturbed. The author notes this is the relied-upon view.

Third Ruling (586): Facing a Mushaf (Quran), a hanging sword, the back of a seated person talking, a candle, or a lamp is not disliked according to the sound narration. The reasoning: Muslims do not worship these objects. The evidence includes the Prophet (peace be upon him) placing a spear in front of him as a sutra while praying on Eid, and the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) lying between the Prophet and the qibla, indicating it is permissible to pray towards or behind an object/person. Also, the practice of Ibn Umar praying behind a seated person.

Fourth Ruling (587): Prostrating on a rug that contains images (of living beings) is not disliked if the worshiper does not prostrate directly on the images. The commentary clarifies that as long as the prostration is not on the picture, it is permissible.

The author follows the typical Hanafi method: ruling, explanation, evidence, and occasional responses to opposing views.

Key Terms
تصاوير (tasawir): Images or pictures, especially of living beings.
سجدة (sajdah): Prostration; the act of placing the forehead on the ground in prayer.

Ruling: Not Makruh to Face Mushaf, Sword, Seated Person, or Lamp
States what is not disliked for the one praying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying towards a Mushaf, sword, seated person, or lamp, and explain the proofs from hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
Facing objects not worshipped during prayer is not makruh.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Thamaratun Najah regarding what objects do NOT make prayer disliked (makruh) when faced during salah. The author clarifies that on the correct view, facing a Mushaf, a suspended sword, the back of a seated person, or a lamp is not makruh. The commentary provides proofs from the Prophet’s practice and from the practice of Ibn Umar. Understanding this ruling helps dispel a common misconception that any object in front of the praying person is disliked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the default assumption
Recognize that the default assumption is that facing objects during prayer might be makruh due to distraction or resemblance to idolatry. The text lists exceptions where it is not makruh.
The act is praying while facing a Mushaf, sword, person's back, or lamp.
2
Analyze the key principle
Understand the underlying principle: objects are not makruh if they are not objects of worship and are not a severe distraction. The commentary states that people do not worship these items, so facing them is permissible.
The principle is derived from the hadith of the spear and the absence of any prohibition.
3
Examine the primary dalil
Study the hadith of Ibn Umar: the Prophet used to have a spear placed before him on Eid and during travel and prayed towards it. This indicates that facing a weapon (and by analogy, other non-worshipped objects) is permissible.
The hadith is from Muslim and Bukhari.
4
Apply qiyas and note the ikhtilaf
Extend the ruling from the spear to a sword, Mushaf, lamp, etc., because the common illa is that they are not worshipped. Note that the text says 'ala al-sahih' because some scholars disagreed and considered it makruh.
Qiyas connects the hadith to other objects. The ikhtilaf is acknowledged but the sound narration is taken.

فصل فيما لا يكره للمصلى
(۵۸۶) ولا التوجه لمصحف او سيف معلق او ظهر قاعد يتحدث او شمع او سراج على الصحيح .
ترجمه : (۵۸۶) اور قرآن مجید یا ٹکی ہوئی تلوار کے سامنے یا بیٹھے ہوئے باتیں کرنے والے کی پشت کی جانب یا شمع یا چراغ کی طرف نماز پڑھنا صحیح روایت میں مکروہ نہیں ہے۔
تشریح : قرآن کریم سامنے ہو ، یاٹکی ہوئی تلوار سامنے ہو اور نماز پڑھے تو مکروہ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ لوگ اس کی عبادت نہیں کرتے اس لئے مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ یوں بھی مسجدوں میں آگے کی کھلی الماری میں قرآن پڑھنے کے لئے رکھا ہوتا ہے۔ آدمی آگے باتیں کر رہا ہو اور پشت کی جانب کوئی نماز پڑھے تو مکروہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ دوسری جانب ہو کر باتیں کر رہے ہیں ۔ یا آگے روشنی کے لئے شمع یا چراغ ہو تو اس کی جانب نماز مکروہ نہیں ہے، کیونکہ لوگ اس کو عبادت کے طور پر سامنے نہیں رکھتے ، بلکہ مجبوری کے درجے میں روشنی کے لئے سامنے رکھتے ہیں۔ متن میں صحیح روایت اس لئے کہا کہ ان مسئلوں میں بعض حضرات کی رائے ہے کہ مکروہ ہے۔
وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے ۔ عن ابن عمر ان رسول الله علم كان اذا خرج يوم العيد أمر بالحربة فتوضع بين يديـه ، فـيـصـلـى اليها و الناس ورائه ، و كان يفعل ذالك في السفر - ( مسلم شریف، باب سترة المصلى والندب الى الصلوة الى سترة ،ص ۱۹۵ نمبر ۱۱۵/۵۰۱ار بخاری شریف، باب حمل العنزة أو الحربة بین یدی الامام یوم العید ، ص ۱۵۶، نمبر ۹۷۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور اپنے سامنے نیزہ رکھتے اور اسکے سامنے نماز پڑھتے ، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ سامنے تلوار یا ہتھیار ہو تو نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے۔اور اسی پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ سامنے قرآن کریم ہو تو بھی نماز جائز ہوگی ، کیونکہ مسلمان انکی عبادت نہیں کرتے ۔ (۲) آدمی سامنے ہو تو اسکے پیچھے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے اسکی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة أن النبی اله كان يصلى من الليل و أنا معترضة بينه و بين القلبة كاعتراض الجنازة - ابن ماجہ ، باب من صلی و بینه و بین القبلی شی ، ص ۱۳۵، نمبر ۹۵۶ ابوداود شریف، باب من قال: المرأة لا تقطع الصلوۃ ، ص نمبر اے ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کوئی آدمی سامنے ہو تو اسکے پیچھے نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ (۳) اس اثر میں ہے بیٹھنے والے کے پیچھے نماز پڑھی ، اثر یہ ہے۔ عن نافع أن ابن عمر كان يقعد رجلا فيصلى خلفه و الناس يمرون بین یدی ذالک الرجل ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، ۵۸ الرجل يستر از اصلی الیہ ام لا ؟ ، ج اول ص ۲۵۰ نمبر ( ۲۸۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ حضرت ابن عمر حضرت نافع جو بیٹھے ہوئے ہوتے انکے پیچھے نماز پڑھتے تھے، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیٹھنے والے کے پیچھے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔
Section on what is not disliked for the one praying. (586) And not facing a mushaf, a suspended sword, the back of a seated person talking, a candle, or a lamp according to the correct (view). Translation: (586) And praying facing the Noble Qur'an, a hanging sword, or the back of a seated person talking, or a candle or lamp is not disliked in the sound narration. Commentary: If the Qur'an is in front, or a hanging sword is in front and one prays, it is not disliked because people do not worship them, so it is not disliked. Likewise, in mosques, the Qur'an is placed in an open shelf in front for recitation. If a person is talking in front and someone prays facing his back, it is not disliked because they are talking turned away. Or if there is a candle or lamp for light in front, praying facing it is not disliked, because people do not place it in front as an act of worship, but out of necessity for light. The text said 'sound narration' because some scholars hold that it is disliked. Proof: (1) Hadith from Ibn Umar that the Prophet used to have a spear placed in front of him on the day of Eid and pray towards it with the people behind, and he did that on journeys. (Muslim, bab sutrat al-musalli, p.195 no.501; Bukhari, bab haml al-'anaza, p.156 no.973). This shows that praying facing a sword or weapon is permissible. By analogy, facing the Qur'an is also permissible because Muslims do not worship it. (2) Praying behind a person: Hadith from Aisha that the Prophet prayed at night while she lay between him and the qibla like a bier. (Ibn Majah, bab man salla wa baynahu wa bayn al-qibla shay', p.135 no.956; Abu Dawud, bab man qala al-mar'a la taqta' al-salah). (3) Athar from Nafi that Ibn Umar would have a man sit and pray behind him while people passed in front of that man. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, bab al-rajul yasturu, vol.1 p.250 no.288).
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof stating that facing certain objects during prayer is not makruh (disliked). The author lists: a Mushaf (Qur'an), a suspended sword, the back of a seated person who is talking, a candle, or a lamp. The Hanafi position is that this is not makruh because these objects are not worshipped; they are either respected (Mushaf, sword) or necessities (light). The commentary clarifies that the text specifies 'on the correct view' because some scholars, possibly from other madhhabs or earlier Hanafis, considered it makruh. The proofs include: (1) The hadith of the spear (hariba) that the Prophet placed before him on Eid and in travel, showing that praying towards a weapon is permissible. By qiyas, the same applies to a sword or Mushaf. (2) The hadith of Aisha showing that praying behind a person (i.e., towards his back) is permissible. (3) The athar of Ibn Umar who would pray behind a seated person. Thus, none of these actions are makruh.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked but not prohibited; reward for avoiding it but no sin for doing it.
صحیح روایت (sahih riwayah): The sound/authentic narration within the Hanafi school, as opposed to weaker reports.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying facing a Mushaf?
A) Makruh
B) Not makruh (permissible)
C) Haram
D) Sunnah

Key Takeaway
Facing a Mushaf, sword, seated person, or lamp during salah is not makruh according to the relied-upon Hanafi view, as these objects are not objects of worship.

Ruling on Prostrating on a Carpet with Images
Ruling on praying on a carpet with pictures when not prostrating on them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prostrating on a carpet with images and apply the condition that distinguishes makruh from not makruh.

Core Idea
Prostrating on an image honors it; treading on it disrespects it — that makes all the difference.

Have you ever wondered about praying on a carpet that has a picture of an animal or human? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling based on the intention behind the contact with the image. This lesson will guide you through the condition that determines whether such prayer is disliked or perfectly fine. We will also examine the prophetic proof that underpins this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is prostrating on a carpet (bisat) that contains images of living beings (taswir). The default ruling is not makruh (not disliked) when the prostration itself does not land on the image.
The ruling changes if the image is directly under the forehead.
2
Locate the Condition
The condition is that the image is not being directly prostrated upon. The text emphasizes 'لم يسجد عليها' (did not prostrate on them).
If one prostrates on the image, the ruling becomes makruh.
3
Find the Dalil
The proof is a hadith from Abu Dawud where Jibril instructed the Prophet to cut the heads of statues and make image-containing curtains into cushions to be trodden upon. This shows that treading on images (disrespect) is permissible.
The hadith is ahad but acceptable in fiqh rulings.
4
Extract the Wajh al-Dalalah
The legal reasoning: just as treading on images is allowed because it is disrespectful, so too is prostration on a carpet with images allowed as long as the prostration itself does not honor the image. Prostrating on the image would be honoring it, hence makruh.
Analogy (qiyas) from cushions to carpets.
5
Note the Ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars might consider it makruh even when not prostrating on the image, and other madhhabs have stricter views. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the one in the text.
Know that this is a legitimate area of difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۸۷) والسجود على بساط فيه تصاوير لم يسجد عليها
ترجمه : (۵۸۷) اور ایسے فرش پر سجدہ کرنا جس میں تصویر ہو، اور تصویر پر سجدہ نہ کرتا ہو تو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔
تشریح : فرش یا کپڑے پر جاندار کی تصویر ہے لیکن تصویر پر سجدہ نہیں کر رہا ہے تو اس کپڑے پر نماز پڑھنا مکروہ نہیں ہے۔
وجه : (۱) نماز کیوقت کپڑے پر یا فرش پر پاؤں رکھے گا تو تصویر کی توہین ہوگی اس لئے مکروہ نہیں ہے ہاں اس تصویر پر سجدہ کرے گا تو اس کی تعظیم ہوگی اس لئے سجدہ کرے تو مکروہ ہوگا ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تصویر کو روند رہا ہو تو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ حدثنا ابو هريرة قال : قال رسول الله الله أتاني جبرائيل فقال لي : أتيتك البارحة فلم يمنعني أن اكون دخـلـت الا أنـه كـان على الباب تماثيل و كان في البيت قرام ستر فيه تماثيل و كان في البيت كلب ، فمر برأس التمثال الذي في باب البيت يقطع فيصير كهيئة الشجرة ومر بالستر فليقطع فليجعل منه و سادتين منبوذتین توطآن و مـر بالكلب فليخرج ففعل رسول الله الله الله (ابوداود شریف ، باب فی الصور ، ص ۵۸۳، نمبر ۴۱۵۸ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تصویر کو روندے تو مکروہ نہیں۔
(587) And prostrating on a carpet containing images without prostrating on them. Translation: (587) And prostrating on a floor covering that has an image, but not prostrating on the image itself, is not disliked. Commentary: If there is an image of a living being on the floor or cloth, but one is not prostrating on the image, then praying on that cloth is not disliked. Proof: (1) During prayer, when one places the feet on the cloth or floor, it is an act of disrespect to the image, so it is not disliked. However, if one prostrates directly on the image, that would be honoring it, so it would be disliked. (2) Hadith: Abu Huraira reported that Jibril told the Prophet to order the removal of images by cutting them and making them into cushions to be trodden upon (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Suwar, p.583 no.4158). This indicates that treading on images is not disliked.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof about prostrating on a surface that contains images. The ruling: if a person prays on a carpet or cloth that has pictures of living beings, but does not prostrate directly onto the picture itself (i.e., the forehead and nose do not touch the image), then the prayer is not makruh. The reason given is that placing the feet on the image is a form of disrespect, which is permissible. However, if one prostrates directly on the image, it would be a form of honor, which is disliked. The proof is a hadith where Jibril instructed to cut the images of living beings and make them into cushions to be trodden upon, showing that disrespecting images (by stepping on them) is not problematic. Thus, the Hanafi position distinguishes between intentional honor and incidental contact.

Key Terms
تصویر (taswir): An image of a living being (animal or human) that has a soul.
بساط (bisat): A floor covering such as a carpet or mat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If one prays on a carpet with a picture of a bird, but the forehead does not touch the picture, what is the ruling?
A) Makruh
B) Not makruh
C) Haram
D) Invalid

Key Takeaway
Praying on a carpet with images is not makruh as long as the image is not directly prostrated upon, because treading on it is a form of disrespect.

Killing Harmful Creatures During Prayer: Hanafi Ruling
Ruling with proof: permissibility of killing harmful creatures in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing a snake or scorpion during prayer and explain the hadith evidence that permits it.

Core Idea
Killing a snake or scorpion in prayer is allowed, even with multiple strikes and turning from qibla, because the Prophet commanded it.

In this lesson, we examine a specific exception to the general rule that excessive actions (amal kathir) invalidate prayer. The Hanafi school, relying on explicit prophetic commands, permits killing a snake or scorpion during prayer even if it involves multiple blows or turning away from the qibla. Understanding this ruling requires knowing both the general principle and its prophetic exception, as well as the intra-Hanafi difference on the limits of permitted action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is killing a snake or scorpion during prayer when one fears harm. The ruling according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) is that it is not makruh (disliked), and the prayer remains valid even if multiple strikes or turning occurs.
Note that the general rule is that excessive movement invalidates prayer; this is an exception.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). Also, a hadith listing five creatures that may be killed even in the Haram supports permissibility.
Both hadiths are ahad (single-transmitter) but considered strong enough for amal.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'iqtilu' is an imperative (amr). In Hanafi usul, amr normally indicates obligation, but the context of prayer shows it indicates permissibility (ibaha) because the Prophet himself permitted it, and it preserves khushu' (focus).
The hadith explicitly says 'in prayer', so it overrides the prohibition of excessive actions.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars, including the author of Nur al-Idah, say even multiple strikes and turning are not makruh. Others argue that if amal kathir occurs or the chest turns completely, the prayer becomes invalid. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is the permissive one, as it is from the apparent narration.
This ikhtilaf shows the range of interpretations within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۸۸) وقتل حية وعقرب خاف اذا هما ولو بضربات وانحراف عن القبلة في الاظهر
ترجمه : (۵۸۸) ایسے سانپ یا بچھو کو قتل کرے جنکے ایڈا کا خوف ہوا تو مکروہ نہیں] اگر چہ کئی مرتبہ مارنا ہو، اور قبلے سے انحراف ہو جائے ، ظاہر روایت میں۔
تشریح : صاحب نور الایضاح کی رائے ہے کہ سانپ ، بچھو کوکئی مرتبہ مارا جس سے عمل کثیر ہو گیا، یا قبلہ سے سینہ پھر گیا تب بھی مکروہ نہیں ہے، کیونکہ حدیث میں اس کو مارنے کا حکم ہے لیکن دوسرے حضرات کی رائے ہے کہ ایڈا کا خوف ہوتو مارنے کی اجازت ہے، لیکن عمل کثیر ہو گیا، یا سینہ قبلہ سے پھر گیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
وجه : (۱) سانپ یا بچھو سامنے ہو تو آدمی کا دل اسکی طرف مشغول رہتا ہے اور خشوع وخضوع ختم ہو جاتا ہے، اور اسکو مار دیا جائے تو خشوع و خضوع باقی رہے گا اسلئے اسکو نماز میں بھی مارنا جائز ہے۔ (۲) حدیث میں اسکا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرۃ قال : قال رسول الله الله اقتلوا الاسودين في الصلوة : الحية و العقرب - (ابوداود شریف، باب العمل فی الصلوۃ ، ص ۱۴۱، نمبر ۹۲۱ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی قتل الاسود بین فی الصلوۃ، ص۱۰۴، نمبر ۳۹۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نماز میں بھی سانپ اور بچھو کو مار سکتے ہو ۔ (۳) اس حدیث میں بھی اسکا ثبوت ہے۔ قالت حفصة قال رسول الله الله : خمس من الدواب لا حرج على من قتلهن : الغراب ، و الحد أ، و الفأرة ، و العقرب ، و الكلب العقور ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب ما ینقتل الحرم من الدواب ،ص ۱۲۹۵ نمبر ۱۸۲۸ر مسلم شریف، باب مایند الحرم وغیرہ قتله من الدواب في المحل والحرم ص ۲۹۸، نمبر ۲۸۶۱/۱۱۹۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ان پانچ جانوروں کو حرم میں بھی مارنا جائز ہے، اس لئے نماز میں بھی مارنا جائز ہوگا۔
(588) And killing a snake and a scorpion when one fears harm from them, even with multiple blows and deviation from the qibla according to the more apparent [narration]. Translation: (588) To kill such a snake or scorpion that one fears harm from, even if one strikes many times, and even if one turns away from the qibla, is not disliked in the apparent narration. Commentary: The author of Nur al-Idah holds that if one strikes a snake or scorpion multiple times, resulting in a large amount of action, or one turns the chest away from the qibla, it is still not disliked because the hadith commands killing them. But other scholars hold that if one fears harm, killing is permitted, but if a large amount of action occurs or the chest turns from the qibla, the prayer becomes invalid. Proof: (1) When a snake or scorpion is in front, the heart becomes occupied with it and khushu' is lost; by killing it, khushu' is preserved, so it is permissible during prayer. (2) Hadith: Abu Huraira reported that the Prophet said: 'Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Amal fi al-Salah, p.141 no.921; Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi Qatl al-Aswadayn fi al-Salah, p.104 no.390). (3) Hadith of Hafsa: The Prophet said: 'Five creatures are not blameworthy to kill: the crow, the kite, the mouse, the scorpion, and the rabid dog.' (Bukhari, Bab ma Yuqtalu min al-Dawab fi al-Haram, p.1295 no.1828; Muslim, Bab ma Yandu al-Haram wa Ghayruhu, p.298 no.2861/1198). Since they may be killed in the Haram, they may be killed in prayer.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding killing harmful creatures during prayer. The Hanafi position, according to the 'zahir al-riwayah' (apparent narration), is that killing a snake or scorpion during prayer is not makruh, even if one needs to strike multiple times or turn away from the qibla. The reason is that the Prophet explicitly commanded killing the 'aswadayn' (the two black ones: snake and scorpion) in prayer, and also mentioned them among five creatures that may be killed in the Haram. Thus, the need to preserve khushu' (focus) and remove distraction overrides the prohibitions against excessive action or turning away. The commentary notes that there is an ikhtilaf: the author of Nur al-Idah (a Hanafi text) allows even multiple strikes and turning; other scholars say that if the action is excessive (amal kathir) or one turns the chest completely, the prayer becomes invalid (fasid). The relied-upon view in this text is the permissive one, as it says 'in al-azhar' (the more apparent). The proofs are explicit hadiths.

Key Terms
عمل کثیر (amal kathir): A large amount of action that nullifies prayer, typically defined as three successive movements in one pillar.
خیف (khauf): Fear of harm from the creature.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), what is the ruling on killing a scorpion during prayer with multiple strikes?
A) It is makruh and prayer becomes invalid.
B) It is permissible and prayer remains valid.
C) It is obligatory but prayer becomes invalid.
D) It is haram because it involves excessive action.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits killing a snake or scorpion during prayer when feared, even with multiple strikes and turning from qibla, based on the prophetic command.

Shaking Clinging Clothing in Ruku: Ruling and Rationale
Ruling on adjusting clinging clothing during ruku

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on shaking clothing in ruku and distinguish between the cases of clinging and non-clinging, including the underlying principle of preserving khushu'.

Core Idea
Shaking clinging clothing in ruku is permissible to preserve concentration, but not recommended as a habit if not clinging.

In prayer, minor movements are often a concern. This lesson addresses a specific scenario: when a garment clings to the body during ruku. The ruling balances permissibility with the goal of maintaining khushu' (focus and humility), a key element in Hanafi prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is shaking one's clothing during ruku when it clings to the body. Determine whether the clothing is actually clinging or not.
2
Apply the ruling for clinging clothing
If the clothing clings, there is no harm (la haraj) in shaking it off. This is permissible (mubah) because it helps maintain khushu'.
The reasoning is based on prioritizing concentration over a minor action.
3
Apply the ruling for non-clinging clothing
If the clothing does not cling, making a habit of repeatedly shaking it is not good (makruh tanzihi). It distracts from humility without necessity.
This is a nuance: occasional shaking may be okay, but habitual repetition without need is discouraged.
4
Understand the rationale: khushu'
The ruling is tied to preserving khushu' (concentration) in prayer. Any minor action that aids concentration is preferable; actions that disrupt it are avoided.
Khushu' is wajib in Hanafi fiqh, but prayer remains valid without it if external actions are correct.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۸۹) اور رکوع میں بدن کے ساتھ کپڑا چمٹ جانے سے اگر اس کو جھٹک دے تو کچھ حرج نہیں۔
تشریح : اگر کپڑا جسم سے چپکا نہ ہوتو بار بارجھٹکنے کی عادت بنانا اچھا نہیں لیکن اگر چپکتا ہوتو جھٹکنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس سے خشوع و خضوع باقی رہے گا۔

Commentary: If the clothing is not clinging to the body, making a habit of repeatedly shaking it is not good. But if it clings, there is no harm in shaking it, because thereby khushu' and khudu' (focus and humility) are preserved.

Commentary
This is a ruling statement regarding adjusting clothing during ruku. The author states that if a garment clings to the body while bowing (ruku), one may shake it off without any harm. The commentary adds a nuance: if the clothing does not actually cling, making a habit of shaking it repeatedly is not good (likely makruh tanzihi). However, if it clings, shaking it is permissible because it helps maintain khushu' (concentration), which is essential in prayer. This is a minor action (amal qalil) that does not invalidate the prayer. The passage does not provide a proof (dalil), but the reasoning is that preserving khushu' is prioritized.

Key Terms
حرج (haraj): Sin, difficulty, or prohibition; here 'no haraj' means no sin or harm.
خشوع و خضوع (khushu' wa khudu'): Focus and humility in prayer; essential for valid prayer.

Killing a Snake or Scorpion During Prayer if Feared: Ruling and Proofs
States ruling that killing feared snake or scorpion in prayer is not disliked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing a feared snake or scorpion during prayer and explain the evidence from hadith and the reasoning behind allowing it even with multiple strikes or deviation from qibla.

Core Idea
Killing a feared snake or scorpion during prayer is not disliked; even multiple strikes and turning from qibla are allowed in the relied-upon view.

A common concern in prayer is whether defensive actions invalidate it. This lesson clarifies that when a harmful animal threatens you during prayer, Hanafi law permits killing it—even if this involves multiple strikes or turning away from the qibla. We will examine the prophetic command that explicitly authorizes this and the reasoning that prioritizes safety and concentration (khushu') over general prohibitions on excessive movement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the exact act being ruled upon (killing a snake or scorpion during prayer when one fears harm) and its legal classification (hukm). The matn states it is 'not disliked' (makruh), which means it is permissible (mubah).
The ruling is specifically conditioned on fear (خاف); if no fear exists, the ruling may differ.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proofs the author cites. The primary evidence is the hadith: 'Iqtulu al-aswadayn fi al-salah' (Kill the two black ones in prayer), reported by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi. A secondary hadith lists the scorpion among five animals that may be killed even in ihram.
Both hadiths are ahad (zanni al-thubut), but they are sufficient to establish permissibility.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the imperative 'iqtulu' proves permissibility. In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub (a command indicates obligation) unless there is a qarina (context) shifting it to ibahah. Here, the command is given for prayer, a context where excessive movement is normally disallowed, indicating permissibility rather than obligation.
Also, the distraction caused by the animal harms khushu', so killing it actually preserves the spirit of prayer.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars argue that excessive action (amal kathir) or turning the chest from qibla invalidates prayer. Their basis is the general principle that such acts nullify prayer. The author mentions this as a differing view.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah and the view of Sahib Nur al-Idah) holds that the prayer remains valid even with multiple strikes and deviation from qibla, as the hadith command overrides these concerns.
This is the position most fatwa authorities follow today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۸۸) وقَتْلُ حَيَّةٍ وَعَقْرَبٍ خَافَ إِذَا هُمَا وَلَوْ بِضَرَبَاتٍ وَانْحِرَافٍ عَنِ الْقِبْلَةِ فِي الْأَظْهَرِ. وجه : (۱) نماز کیوقت کپڑے پر یا فرش پر پاؤں رکھے گا تو تصویر کی توہین ہوگی اس لئے مکروہ نہیں ہے ہاں اس تصویر پر سجدہ کرے گا تو اس کی تعظیم ہوگی اس لئے سجدہ کرے تو مکروہ ہوگا ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تصویر کو روند رہا ہو تو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ حدثنا ابو هريرة قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أتاني جبرائيل فقال لي : أتيتك البارحة فلم يمنعني أن أكون دخلت إلا أنه كان على الباب تماثيل و كان في البيت قرام ستر فيه تماثيل و كان في البيت كلب ، فمر برأس التمثال الذي في باب البيت يقطع فيصير كهيئة الشجرة ومر بالستر فليقطع فليجعل منه وسادتين منبوذتين توطآن ومر بالكلب فليخرج ففعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم (أبو داود شريف، باب في الصور، ص ۵۸۳، نمبر ۴۱۵۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تصویر کو روندے تو مکروہ نہیں۔ ترجمه : (۵۸۸) ایسے سانپ یا بچھو کو قتل کرے جنکے ایذا کا خوف ہوا تو مکروہ نہیں اگر چہ کئی مرتبہ مارنا ہو، اور قبلے سے انحراف ہو جائے، ظاہر روایت میں۔ تشریح : صاحب نور الایضاح کی رائے ہے کہ سانپ، بچھو کو کئی مرتبہ مارا جس سے عمل کثیر ہو گیا، یا قبلہ سے سینہ پھر گیا تب بھی مکروہ نہیں ہے، کیونکہ حدیث میں اس کو مارنے کا حکم ہے لیکن دوسرے حضرات کی رائے ہے کہ ایذا کا خوف ہو تو مارنے کی اجازت ہے، لیکن عمل کثیر ہو گیا، یا سینہ قبلہ سے پھر گیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ وجه : (۱) سانپ یا بچھو سامنے ہو تو آدمی کا دل اسکی طرف مشغول رہتا ہے اور خشوع وخضوع ختم ہو جاتا ہے، اور اسکو مار دیا جائے تو خشوع و خضوع باقی رہے گا اسلئے اسکو نماز میں بھی مارنا جائز ہے۔ (۲) حدیث میں اسکا ثبوت ہے۔ عن أبی هريرة قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اقتلوا الأسودين في الصلاة : الحية والعقرب - (أبو داود شريف، باب العمل في الصلاة، ص ۱۴۱، نمبر ۹۲۱ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في قتل الأسودين في الصلاة، ص۱۰۴، نمبر ۳۹۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نماز میں بھی سانپ اور بچھو کو مار سکتے ہو ۔ (۳) اس حدیث میں بھی اسکا ثبوت ہے۔ قالت حفصة قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : خمس من الدواب لا حرج على من قتلهن : الغراب، والحدأة، والفأرة، والعقرب، والكلب العقور ۔ (بخاری شریف، باب ما يقتل الحرم من الدواب، ص ۱۲۹۵ نمبر ۱۸۲۸، مسلم شریف، باب ما يندب الحرم وغیره قتله من الدواب في المحل والحرم، ص ۲۹۸، نمبر ۲۸۶۱/۱۱۹۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ان پانچ جانوروں کو حرم میں بھی مارنا جائز ہے، اس لئے نماز میں بھی مارنا جائز ہوگا۔
(588) And killing a snake or scorpion when he fears them, even with strikes and deviation from the qibla, in the apparent narration. Aspect (1): When praying, if he places his feet on a cloth or mat that has an image, it is not disliked because it is disrespect to the image; but if he prostrates on it, it is disliked because it is veneration. (2) This hadith indicates that trampling an image is not disliked. Narrated Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Jibril came to me and said: I came to you last night and nothing prevented me from entering except that there were statues at the door, and there was a curtain with images in the house, and there was a dog in the house. So command that the head of the statue at the door be cut off so it becomes like a tree, and the curtain be cut and made into two cushions to be trampled, and the dog be expelled. So the Messenger of Allah did so (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Suwar, p. 583, no. 4158). This hadith indicates that trampling an image is not disliked. Translation: (588) Killing a snake or scorpion that one fears is not disliked, even if he strikes multiple times and deviates from the qibla, in the apparent narration. Commentary: Sahib Nur al-Idah holds that killing a snake or scorpion even with multiple strikes (excessive action) or turning the chest from qibla is still not disliked because of the command in the hadith. But other scholars hold that if fear exists, killing is permitted, but if excessive action occurs or the chest turns from qibla, the prayer becomes invalid. Aspect (1): When a snake or scorpion is present, the person's heart is distracted towards it and khushu' and khudu' are lost; if he kills it, khushu' remains, so it is permissible to kill it in prayer. (2) The hadith proves this: Abu Hurairah reported: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-‘Amal fi al-Salah, p. 141, no. 921; Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi Qatl al-Aswadayn fi al-Salah, p. 104, no. 390). This hadith indicates that you can kill a snake and scorpion even in prayer. (3) This hadith also proves it: Hafsah reported: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Five animals for which there is no blame on one who kills them: the crow, the kite, the mouse, the scorpion, and the biting dog.' (Bukhari, Bab ma Yuqtal al-Haram min al-Dawab, p. 1295, no. 1828; Muslim, Bab ma Yandabu al-Haram wa Ghayruhu Qatlahu min al-Dawab fi al-Muhill wa al-Haram, p. 298, no. 2861/1198). This hadith indicates that it is permissible to kill these five animals even in the Haram, so it is also permissible in prayer.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the permissibility of killing a snake or scorpion during prayer if one fears harm from them. The matn states that it is not disliked (makruh) even if it requires multiple strikes or causes deviation from the qibla, according to the zahir al-riwayah. The commentary then provides two faces of reasoning: first, that the distraction of the animal breaks khushu', so killing it restores concentration; second, prophetic hadiths explicitly command killing the 'two black ones' (snake and scorpion) in prayer, and another hadith lists them among five animals that may be killed even in ihram. The author then discusses a difference: according to Sahib Nur al-Idah, even if the action becomes excessive (amal kathir) or one turns away from qibla, it is still not disliked because of the general command. However, other scholars hold that if fear exists, killing is permitted, but if excessive action occurs or one turns away, the prayer becomes invalid. The relied-upon position is that of the zahir al-riwayah and Nur al-Idah, as the hadith offers a general license.

Key Terms
حية (hayyah): Snake, one of the two harmful animals mentioned
عقرب (aqrab): Scorpion, the other harmful animal
عمل كثير (amal kathir): Excessive action that invalidates prayer according to some scholars
خشوع (khushu'): Humility and focus in prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is not disliked; the prayer remains valid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits killing a feared snake or scorpion during prayer based on an explicit hadith, and this permission extends even to multiple strikes and turning from qibla in the relied-upon view.

Shaking the Garment During Bowing to Prevent Sticking
Ruling with proof via analogy to pebble-wiping hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on shaking the garment during salah when it sticks to the body, and identify the evidence (dalil) and reasoning (qiyas) behind it.

Core Idea
Shaking the garment to remove sticking is permissible by analogy to wiping pebbles once.

When a garment sticks to the body during bowing (ruku), it can disturb khushu'. The Hanafi school, relying on a prophetic hadith, permits a single shake to remove it. This lesson examines the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling
Identify the exact ruling: 'no harm' (la ba's) in shaking the garment if it sticks during ruku. This indicates permissibility (ibaha).
The ruling is conditioned on necessity—habitual shaking without sticking is discouraged.
2
Identify the Dalil
The author cites the hadith of Miqdad (and Abu Dharr) about wiping pebbles during prayer. The Prophet permitted a single wipe if necessary.
The hadith is ahad (single narration) but accepted for such rulings.
3
Trace the Qiyas (Analogy)
Both removing pebbles and shaking the garment are small, necessary movements to maintain focus (khushu'). The ʿillah (cause) is necessity and minimal action.
The analogy is clear: if one wipe is allowed, one shake is similarly allowed.
4
Note the Condition and Limitation
The commentator adds that if the garment is not sticking, making a habit of shaking is not good. The permissibility is only when the garment actually sticks.
Excessive movement beyond necessity would be makruh.
5
Apply the Ruling
In practice, a worshipper may gently shake (nafd) the stuck garment once during ruku. Multiple shakes or habitual shaking without sticking is discouraged.
This ruling helps preserve khushu' without nullifying prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵۸۹) ولا بأس بنفض ثوبه كيلا يلتصق بجسده في الركوع. وجه : اس حدیث میں اس کا اشاره ہے۔ عن معیقیب قال سألت رسول الله عن مسح الحصى في الصلاة فقال صلى الله عليه وسلم إن كنت لا بد فاعلا فمرة واحدة . و في حديث آخر عن أبي ذر عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال إذا قام أحدكم إلى الصلاة فلا يمسح الحصى فإن الرحمة تواجهه (ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء في كراهية مسح الحصى في الصلاة ص ۸۷، نمبر ۳۷۹، أبو داؤد شریف، باب في مسح الحصى في الصلاة، ص ۱۴۳، نمبر ۹۴۵/۹۴۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مجبوری کے درجے میں کنکری کو ہٹانا جائز ہے تو کپڑے کو جھٹکنا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ لغت نفض : جھٹکنا ۔ یا تصق : چپکتا ہو۔ ترجمه : (۵۸۹) اور رکوع میں بدن کے ساتھ کپڑا چمٹ جانے سے اگر اس کو جھٹک دے تو کچھ حرج نہیں۔ تشریح : اگر کپڑا جسم سے چپکا نہ ہو تو بار بار جھٹکنے کی عادت بنانا اچھا نہیں لیکن اگر چپکتا ہو تو جھٹکنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس سے خشوع و خضوع باقی رہے گا۔
(589) And there is no harm in shaking his garment so that it does not stick to his body during bowing. Aspect: This hadith indicates it. From Miqdad: He asked the Messenger of Allah about wiping pebbles during prayer, and he said: 'If you must do it, then once.' And in another hadith from Abu Dharr from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: 'When one of you stands for prayer, let him not wipe pebbles, for mercy faces him.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi Karahiyat Masah al-Hasa fi al-Salah, p. 87, no. 379; Abu Dawud, Bab fi Masah al-Hasa fi al-Salah, p. 143, no. 945/946). From this hadith it is understood that removing pebbles in case of necessity is permissible, so shaking the garment is also permissible. Lexicon: Nafd: shaking. Yaltafiq: sticks. Translation: (589) And during bowing, if the garment sticks to the body and he shakes it off, there is no harm. Commentary: If the garment is not sticking, making a habit of repeatedly shaking it is not good. But if it sticks, there is no harm in shaking it, because khushu' and khudu' remain.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of shaking one's garment during bowing (ruku') if it sticks to the body. The matn states there is no harm in it. The commentary explains that if the garment is not sticking, making a habit of repeatedly shaking it is not good, but if it sticks, shaking it once is fine to maintain khushu'. The proof is via analogy (qiyas) from the hadith about wiping pebbles (hasah) during prayer, where one wipe is allowed if necessary. Similarly, shaking the garment is allowed to avoid distraction.

Key Terms
نفض (nafd): Shaking or flicking the garment to remove dirt or adjust it
التصاق (iltisaq): Sticking of the garment to the body, causing distraction

Wiping the Forehead from Dust After Prayer or When Needed
Ruling that wiping forehead from dust is not disliked after prayer or before if it disturbs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping dust from the forehead during and after prayer and identify the condition of necessity.

Core Idea
Wiping dust from the forehead is not disliked after prayer or during prayer if it disturbs prayer.

We often see people wiping dust from their forehead after prostration. Is this allowed during prayer? This lesson clarifies that after prayer it is perfectly fine, and during prayer it is permitted only if the dust causes harm or distraction. We will examine the textual proofs from the Quran, Hadith, and the sayings of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
What is the act being discussed? Wiping dust or grass from the forehead. The ruling is 'not disliked' (mubah) after prayer, and also not disliked during prayer if it harms or distracts.
2
Understand the Two Scenarios
After prayer: no restriction because prayer is over. During prayer: only allowed if there is harm or distraction. Otherwise, it is makruh.
The commentary specifies 'without excessive action' during prayer.
3
Examine the First Proof
The saying of Ibn Abbas: 'He should not wipe his face from dust during prayer until he recites tashahhud and says salam.' This implies that after salam it is allowed (mafhum al-mukhalafah).
This is a Companion saying, considered zanni al-thubut.
4
Examine the Second Proof
The hadith of Miqdad about wiping pebbles during prayer: the Prophet allowed one wipe if necessary. The same applies to dust: if it causes harm, one may wipe once.
Qiyas (analogy) between pebbles and dust, as both can be a source of distraction.
5
Apply the Ruling
Given a scenario, determine if wiping is allowed. For example, after Asr prayer, a person wipes dust: allowed. During Zuhr, dust on forehead causes itching: allowed once if it disturbs concentration.

(590) And there is no dislike in wiping his forehead from dust or grass after finishing the prayer, nor before finishing if it harms him or distracts him from the prayer. Commentary: After finishing the prayer, wiping dust from the forehead or grass from the garment is not disliked, because he is no longer in prayer and it is not contrary to piety. Similarly, if during prayer dust disturbs his prostration or causes loss of khushu' and khudu', then without excessive action, wiping dust is not disliked. Aspect (1): Ibn Abbas said: 'He should not wipe his face from dust during prayer until he recites tashahhud and says salam.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab la Yamsahu Wajhahu min al-Turab fi al-Salah hatta Yusallim, vol. 2, p. 206, no. 3553). This saying of a Companion indicates that before salam he should not wipe dust, meaning after salam he may wipe dust or grass. (2) From Miqdad: He asked the Messenger of Allah about wiping pebbles during prayer, and he said: 'If you must do it, then once.' And in another hadith from Abu Dharr from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'When one of you stands for prayer, let him not wipe pebbles, for mercy faces him.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi Karahiyat Masah al-Hasa fi al-Salah, p. 87, no. 379; Abu Dawud, Bab fi Masah al-Hasa fi al-Salah, p. 143, no. 945/946). From this hadith it is understood that removing pebbles in case of necessity is permissible, so if dust causes harm, removing it is also permissible. Translation: (590) And it is not disliked to wipe the forehead from dust or grass after the prayer, and before finishing if it harms or distracts.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage covers wiping dust or grass from the forehead after prayer or during prayer if it causes harm or distraction. The matn says it is not disliked after prayer, nor before prayer if it harms or distracts. The commentary explains that after prayer it is permissible as one is no longer in prayer. During prayer, if the dust disturbs sujud or khushu', wiping without excessive action is allowed. The proof is from a saying of Ibn Abbas that one should not wipe the face until after tashahhud and salam, implying after prayer it is fine, and from the hadith about wiping pebbles, which allows one wipe out of necessity. The analogy is that if pebbles may be moved for necessity, dust may also be wiped.

Key Terms
مسح (masah): Wiping or removing dust from the forehead or face
جبهة (jabhah): Forehead, the part that touches the ground in prostration

Key Takeaway

Looking with the Eyes in Prayer: Ruling and Nuance
Ruling on looking in prayer with explanation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between iltifat al-wajh (turning the face) and iltifat al-'ayn (moving the eyes) in prayer and state the Hanafi ruling for each.

Core Idea
Moving your eyes in salah is not disliked, but turning your face is makruh; both lessen khushu'.

Prayer demands focus and reverence toward Allah. The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between two types of physical movement during prayer: turning the entire face away from the qibla, and merely shifting the gaze by moving the eyes. This lesson examines the ruling for each based on the matn and its commentary, supported by a hadith of Sayyiduna Abu Bakr al-Siddiq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being ruled upon
The act is 'looking' in prayer. The matn states that looking (with the eyes) is not disliked. Determine what specific action is being discussed.
The Arabic term 'نظر' (nazar) here means looking with the eyes, not turning the face.
2
Distinguish between two types of turning
The commentary clarifies two forms of iltifat: turning the face (iltifat al-wajh) and turning only the eyes (iltifat al-'ayn). Recognize that they have different rulings.
Iltifat al-wajh is explicitly makruh; iltifat al-'ayn is not makruh but still opposes khushu'.
3
State the Hanafi ruling for each type
For turning the face: makruh tanzihi. For moving only the eyes: not disliked (mubah), but it is against the perfection of khushu'.
Khushu' is an essential aspect of prayer, so while not forbidden, avoiding such movements is recommended.
4
Examine the prophetic proof (dalil)
The commentary cites the hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd where Abu Bakr moved his eyes (iltifat bil 'ayn) to see the Prophet during prayer, without turning his face. This shows the permissibility of such action.
The hadith is from Sahih Bukhari. Abu Bakr's action was during a necessity (excessive clapping), but it indicates the basic permissibility.
5
Appreciate the nuance regarding khushu'
Although the action is not makruh, it detracts from khushu' and khudu'. Therefore, the ideal is to avoid even eye movements unless necessary.
This reflects the Hanafi concern for the spirit of prayer beyond the bare minimum of validity.

This passage addresses looking in prayer. The matn states that looking with the eye without turning the face is not disliked. The commentary clarifies that turning the face in prayer is makruh, but merely moving the eyes (iltifat bil 'ayn) is not makruh, although it goes against the perfection of khushu'. The proof is the action of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq who during prayer turned his eyes to see the Prophet while not turning his face. The hadith is from Bukhari, though the text cuts off.

The Ruling on Shaking One's Garment During Prayer
Chapter opening and first ruling on permissible actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on permissible minor movements during prayer by distinguishing between necessary and unnecessary actions, and explain the qiyas from wiping pebbles to shaking the garment.

Core Idea
A minor movement in prayer is permissible when needed for concentration — shaking a garment to avoid sticking is allowed.

This passage opens a chapter on acts not disliked for the worshiper. The first ruling addresses a practical concern: during bowing, one's garment may stick to the body. The author rules that shaking it is not disliked. But what is the proof? The text draws on a hadith about wiping pebbles, extending the same logic to garment shaking. In this lesson, we will trace the chain of proof and understand the principle of minor movements in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is shaking one's garment to prevent sticking during ruku. The ruling: not disliked (mubah).
The phrase 'لا بأس' indicates permissibility, not obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadith: the hadith of Mu'aiqib on wiping pebbles (permission if necessary, only once) and the hadith of Abu Dharr prohibiting wiping pebbles (mercy faces the worshiper).
The first hadith provides conditional permission; the second warns against unnecessary movement.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The conditional permission ('if you must') shows that eliminating disturbance is allowed. The prohibition in the second hadith is for unnecessary movement. So shaking the garment, when it disturbs, falls under the same permission.
The illa (effective cause) is the need to remove a disturbance to khushu’.
4
Identify the qiyas
The author draws qiyas: as wiping pebbles is allowed when they disturb, shaking a sticking garment is allowed when it disturbs.
Thus the ruling is established by analogy from a directly permitted act.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
While the Hanafi school permits it, some Shafi'i scholars consider it makruh if done deliberately without need. The mufta bihi is permissibility when needed.
This is a legitimate difference based on interpretation of the conditional phrase.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما لا يكره للمصلى (۵۸۹) ولا بأس بنفض ثوبه كيلا يلتصق بجسده في الركوع وجه : اس حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن معیقیب قال سألت رسول الله عن مسح الحصى في الصلوة فقال صلى الله ان كنت لا بد فاعلا فمرة واحدة . و في حديث آخر عن ابي ذر عن النبي عله قال اذا قام احدكم الى الصلوة فلا يمسح الحصى فان الرحمة تواجهه ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی کراھیة مسح الحصی فی الصلوۃ ص ۸۷، نمبر ۳۷۹ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب فی مسح الحصى في الصلوۃ ، ص ۱۴۳، نمبر ۹۴۵/۹۴۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مجبوری کے درجے میں کنکری کو ہٹانا جائز ہے تو کپڑے کو جھٹکنا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ لغت نفض : جھٹکنا ۔ یا تصق : چپکتا ہو۔
Chapter on what is not disliked for the worshiper (589): There is no harm in shaking his garment so that it does not stick to his body during bowing. Reason: This hadith indicates it: From Mu'aiqib who said: I asked the Messenger of Allah about wiping pebbles during prayer, and he said, 'If you must do it, then only once.' And in another hadith from Abu Dharr from the Prophet, he said: 'When one of you stands for prayer, he should not wipe the pebbles, for mercy faces him.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on the dislike of wiping pebbles during prayer, p.87, no.379; Abu Dawud, chapter on wiping pebbles during prayer, p.143, no.945/946). From this hadith it is understood that in a state of necessity, removing pebbles is permissible, so shaking the garment is also permissible. Lexicon: nafd means to shake; yaltaṣiqu means sticks.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the chapter on what is not disliked for the worshiper. The first ruling: shaking one's garment to prevent it from sticking during ruku is not disliked. The author provides proof from two hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted wiping pebbles once if necessary, and forbade it otherwise. By analogy (qiyas), if pebbles can be removed when they disturb, then shaking the garment to avoid sticking is similarly permitted when it disturbs. The Urdu commentary clarifies that this permission is only when there is genuine need; otherwise, unnecessary movements are discouraged. The glossary defines key terms: 'nafd' (shaking) and 'yaltaṣiqu' (sticks).

Key Terms

یلتصق (yaltaṣiqu): To stick to

Looking with the Corner of the Eye in Prayer
Ruling on glancing without turning the face

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible glancing (without turning the face) and impermissible turning of the face during prayer according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Glancing without turning the face is permissible but diminishes khushu; turning the face is makruh.

Maintaining focus (khushu) is essential in prayer. While turning the face away is clearly disliked, what about a quick glance with the eyes? This lesson explores the Hanafi distinction between turning the face and merely glancing, supported by the actions of the Prophet's Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? (Turning the face vs. glancing with eyes). Determine the hukm for each: turning is makruh, glancing without turning is not disliked (la ba's) but goes against khushu.
The key term is 'muq' – corner of the eye, i.e., peripheral glance.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari: (1) Abu Bakr glanced at the Prophet during prayer without turning his face, (2) The Prophet looked at the qibla to remove sputum. These show permissibility of glancing.
Both are ahad hadith, zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How do these hadith prove the ruling? Abu Bakr's action did not draw rebuke, indicating permissibility. The Prophet's deliberate looking at the qibla further supports that such glances are not prohibited.
The inference is from the absence of prohibition (sukut al-shar').
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools consider any looking away as makruh. The Hanafi school differentiates between turning (makruh) and merely glancing (permissible but better avoided).
The practical difference: a slight eye movement is tolerated; turning the neck is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۹۱) ولا بالنظر بموق عينيه من غير تحويل الوجه . تشریح نماز میں منہ پھرا کر دیکھنا مکروہ ہے البتہ منہ پھرائے بغیر نظر گھما کر دیکھنا مکروہ نہیں ہے، البتہ یہ خشوع خضوع کے منافی ہے وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت ابو بکر نے نظر گھما کر حضور کودیکھا . عن سهل ابن سعد الساعدي ..... و كان ابو بكر لا يلتفت في صلاته فلما اكثر الناس التصفيق التفت فرأى رسول الله الله ( بخاری شریف، باب من دخل ليوم الناس فجاء الامام الاول، ص ۱۱۱ نمبر ۶۸۴) (۲) عن عمر انه قال رأى النبي لا نخامة في قبلة فجاء صل الله المسجد و هو يصلى بين يدى الناس فحتها - ( بخاری شریف، باب هل يلتفت لامرینزل به؟ اویری شیئا او بصاقا فی القبلة ص ۱۲۲، نمبر ۳ ۷۵ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے قبلے کی طرف دیکھا۔ لغت : موق : آنکھ کا کنارہ، گوشه چشم ۔

Explanation: Turning the face during prayer is disliked, but glancing without turning the face is not disliked, although it goes against khushu (humility). Proof: (1) In this hadith, Abu Bakr glanced at the Prophet without turning. From Sahl ibn Sa'd al-Sa'idi: Abu Bakr did not turn his face in prayer, but when many people clapped, he turned and saw the Messenger of Allah. (Bukhari, chapter on someone who enters for the prayer and the imam comes first, p.111, no.684). (2) From Umar: He said, 'The Prophet saw sputum on the qibla wall, so he came while praying before the people and scraped it off.' (Bukhari, chapter on whether one turns for something that comes down, p.122, no.375). This hadith shows that the Prophet looked toward the qibla. Lexicon: muq means corner of the eye.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on looking during prayer. It distinguishes between turning the face (which is makruh) and merely glancing with the eyes without turning the face (which is not makruh but undesirable because it contradicts khushu). The proofs: the hadith of Abu Bakr who glanced without turning, and the hadith of Umar that the Prophet looked at the qibla to remove sputum. The Hanafi position is that turning the face is makruh tahrimi (close to haram), while glancing without turning is makruh tanzihi or merely against the sunnah of khushu. The key term 'muq' (corner of the eye) is defined.

Praying on Carpets, Mats, and Felts
Ruling on permissible prayer surfaces with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying on carpets and mats, identify the preferred surface, and explain the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Praying on carpets is permissible, but the ground is better for khushu.

Many Muslims pray in homes or mosques with carpets, mats, or felts. Is this valid? Should we seek to pray on bare earth? This short passage from our Hanafi text clarifies the matter: it is permissible, but not optimal. The hadith of the Prophet ﷺ show he prayed on a small palm-leaf mat (khumrah) and a reed mat, establishing permissibility while also showing that direct earth is superior for humility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the opening line: 'There is no harm in praying on carpets, mats, and felts.' This tells us the permissibility. Note the phrase 'لا بأس' (la ba's) which in Hanafi fiqh indicates that the action is permissible (mubah) and not disliked.
Contrast with 'makruh' or 'haram' which would indicate prohibition.
2
Note the Preferred Act
The text immediately adds: 'But it is better to pray on the ground or on what grows from it.' This shows that while permissible, the sunnah is to pray on earth (or natural materials like reed mats) for greater khushu.
The Urdu commentary emphasizes khushu (humility) as the reason.
3
Locate the Proof (Dalil)
Two hadith from Sunan Abu Dawud are cited. The first from Maimuna: the Prophet ﷺ prayed on a khumrah (small mat). The second from Anas: he prayed on a reed mat (bisaat). These establish the permissibility of praying on a barrier between the ground and the forehead.
The khumrah was a small mat made of palm leaves, used specifically for prostration.
4
Derive the Ruling from the Dalil
The Prophet's action (fi'l) is a proof of permissibility. If it were disliked, he would not have done it consistently. The Hanafi school takes this as evidence that praying on any clean covering is valid, though the best is the ground.
The hadith are ahad (single-transmitter), so they give zanni proof, which suffices for a mubah ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۹۲) ولا بأس بالصلوة على الفُرش والبسط واللبود . والافضل الصلوة على الارض او على ما تُنبته تشریح : زمین پر نماز پڑھنا افضل ہے کیونکہ اس میں خشوع و خضوع زیادہ ہے لیکن اگر فرش پر یا بچھونے پر بالبادے پر نماز پڑھ لے تو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ وجه : (۱) حدثتني ميمونة بنت الحارث قالت كان رسول الله الله يصلى و انا حذائه و انا حائض و ربما أصابتني ثوبه اذا سجد و كان يصلى على الخمرة - (ابوداود شریف، باب الصلوة على الخمرة ص ۱۰۵، نمبر ۶۵۶) عن انس بن مالک ان النبی الله الله كان يزور ام سلیم فتدركه الصلاة احيانا فيصلى على بساط لنا و هو حصير تنضحه بالماء. (ابوداود شریف، باب الصلوة على الحصیر، ص ۱۰۵ نمبر ۶۵۸) ان دونوں حدیثوں میں ہے کہ چٹائی اور بستر پر نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے۔
Translation (592): There is no harm in praying on carpets, mats, and felts. But it is better to pray on the ground or on what grows from it. Explanation: Praying on the ground is better because it has more humility and submissiveness. However, if one prays on a carpet, bedding, or felt, it is not disliked. Proof: (1) Maimuna bint al-Harith narrated: The Messenger of Allah used to pray while I was opposite him, and I was menstruating. Sometimes his garment touched me when he prostrated, and he used to pray on a khumrah (small mat). (Abu Dawud, chapter on praying on a khumrah, p.105, no.656). From Anas ibn Malik: The Prophet used to visit Umm Sulaim, and sometimes the prayer would catch him, so he would pray on a mat of ours which was a reed mat sprinkled with water. (Abu Dawud, chapter on praying on a mat, p.105, no.658). These two hadith show that praying on a mat or bedding is permissible.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the ground covering for prayer. It states that praying on carpets, mats, or felts is not disliked, but the best is to pray directly on the ground or on earth-grown materials (like a reed mat). The Urdu commentary explains that ground prayer enhances khushu. The proofs are the hadith of Maimuna that the Prophet prayed on a khumrah (small mat) and the hadith of Anas that he prayed on a reed mat. These indicate permissibility. The Hanafi position: it is permissible (mubah) to pray on any clean surface, but sunnah to pray on the ground when possible.

Key Terms
فرش (furush): Carpets or floor coverings
خمرة (khumrah): A small mat made from palm leaves used for prostration

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred surface for prayer according to this passage?
A) Carpet.
B) A felt mat.
C) The ground or earth-grown items.
D) Any surface is equally preferred.

Key Takeaway
Praying on carpets, mats, or felts is permissible (mubah), but praying on the ground is better for humility (khushu).

Ruling: Repeating a Surah in Nafl Prayer
Ruling on repeating a surah in nafl prayer with evidence from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeating a surah in nafl prayer and identify the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
In nafl prayer, you may repeat the same surah or recite multiple surahs in one rakah — complete freedom in recitation.

This lesson addresses a question that often arises: is it permissible to recite the same surah in both rakahs of a voluntary prayer? The Hanafi school, based on clear prophetic practice, affirms flexibility. We will examine the primary evidence from two hadiths cited in the classical text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is repeating a surah in nafl or reciting multiple surahs in one rakah. The ruling is mubah (permissible).
The Urdu commentary clarifies that one may lengthen the prayer as desired.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The text cites two hadiths: (1) The Prophet recited Surah al-Zalzalah in both rakahs of Fajr (Abu Dawud). (2) The Prophet recited multiple surahs in one rakah of night prayer (Muslim).
The first hadith is directly quoted; the second is referenced but not fully quoted.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates permissibility. The fact that he repeated the same surah shows it is allowed; the second hadith shows lengthy recitation with multiple surahs is also allowed.
The Hanafi principle: the Prophet's action establishes permissibility unless there is evidence of prohibition.
4
Confirm the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school takes this as mubah (permissible) in nafl. There is no dispute among the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). The ruling applies to both repetition and multiple surahs in one rakah.
In fard prayer, repetition is also permissible but may be considered makruh tanzihi if done without reason.

ترجمه : (۵۹۳) ولا بأس بتكرار السورة في الركعتين من النفل . تشریح : ایک ہی سورت کو نفل کی دونوں رکعتوں میں پڑھے تو اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ اور دوسرا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ایک رکعت میں دو سورتیں پڑھ لے تب بھی کوئی حرج نہیں ہے، کیونکہ یہ اپنی نماز جتنی چاہے لمبی کرے۔ وجه :(۱) عن معاذ بن عبد الله الجهنى ان رجلا من جهينة اخبره انه سمع النبي الله يقرأ في الصبح اذا صلى الله زلزلت الارض في الركعتين كلتيهما فلا ادرى انسى رسول الله ل ام قرأذالک عمدا ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب الرجل يعيد سورة واحدة في الركعتين ،ص۱۲۶ نمبر ۸۱۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دونوں رکعتوں میں ایک ہی سورت پڑھی۔(۲) عن حذيفة قال صليت مع النبي عل الله ذات ليلة فافتتح البقرة فقلت يركع عند المأة ثم مضى فقلت يصلى بها في ركعة فمضى فقلت يركع بها ثم افتتح النساء فقرأها ثم افتتح آل عمران فقرأها يقرأ مترسلا ۔(مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب تطویل القرآة في صلاة الليل ، ص ۱۳۱۵، نمبر ۷۲ ۱۸۱۴/۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تہجد کی نماز میں ایک رکعت
Translation (593): There is no harm in repeating a surah in the two rakahs of nafl. Explanation: If one recites the same surah in both rakahs of nafl, there is no harm. Another meaning is that if one recites two surahs in one rakah, there is also no harm, because one may lengthen his prayer as he wishes. Proof: (1) From Mu'adh ibn Abdullah al-Juhani that a man from Juhaynah told him that he heard the Prophet reciting 'Idha zulzilat al-ard' in both rakahs of Fajr, and he said, 'I do not know if he forgot or did it intentionally.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on a man repeating one surah in two rakahs, p.126, no.816). This hadith shows that he recited the same surah in both rakahs. (2) From Hudhayfah: I prayed with the Prophet one night, and he started with al-Baqarah, so I thought he would bow at the hundredth verse, but he continued. Then I thought he would complete it in one rakah, but he continued. Then I thought he would bow after completing it, then he started al-Nisa and recited it, then he started Al Imran and recited it slowly. (Muslim, chapter on the recommendation of lengthening recitation in night prayer, p.1315, no.1814/72). This hadith shows that in tatajjur prayer, one rakah
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on recitation in nafl prayer. It states that there is no harm in repeating the same surah in both rakahs of nafl, nor in reciting multiple surahs in one rakah. The Urdu commentary adds that one may lengthen the prayer by reciting more. The proofs: the hadith of Mu'adh that the Prophet recited the same surah (al-Zalzala) in both rakahs of Fajr (though Fajr is fard, the principle applies), and the hadith of Hudhayfah that the Prophet recited many surahs in one rakah during night prayer. The Hanafi position: it is permissible, though it may be better to recite different surahs in fard prayer for variety. The key ruling is that in nafl, the worshiper has more freedom in recitation.

Key Terms
تكرار (tikrar): Repetition of a surah
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is not allowed.
B) It is allowed because one may lengthen the prayer.
C) It is only allowed in the first rakah.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
In nafl prayer, repeating a surah or reciting multiple surahs in one rakah is fully permissible; the worshiper may lengthen their prayer as desired.

Permissible Actions in Prayer: Carpets and Repeating Surahs
Explaining two rulings on permissible actions in prayer with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying on carpets and repeating surahs in nafl, and identify the hadith evidence that supports these rulings.

Core Idea
Praying on carpets and repeating surahs in nafl are permissible; the Prophet's practice confirms it.

This passage clarifies two actions that are not disliked in prayer: praying on manufactured surfaces like carpets and repeating the same surah in nafl. While the preferred practice is to pray on natural ground, the Hanafi school permits these actions based on clear Prophetic precedent. Let's examine the rulings and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate the two distinct rulings in the passage: (1) praying on carpets, spreads, and felt is not disliked; (2) repeating a surah in both rak'ahs of nafl is not disliked. Note the Arabic phrase 'la ba'sa' (no harm) indicating permissibility.
These are independent rulings under the same chapter heading.
2
Examine the first ruling's evidence
Read the hadith of Maimunah and Anas. The Prophet prayed on a khumrah (small mat) and on a mat belonging to Umm Sulaym. These actions demonstrate permissibility in the Hanafi usul, as the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates permissibility (ibahah).
The hadith are from Abu Dawood, classified as ahad, but the meaning is clear.
3
Examine the second ruling's evidence
Read the hadith of Mu'adh and Hudhayfah. The Prophet recited the same surah in both rak'ahs of Fajr (according to the report) and lengthened night prayer by reciting multiple surahs. This shows flexibility in nafl recitation.
The passage also allows reciting two surahs in one rak'ah.
4
Understand the afdal and the permissibility
Note that while praying on earth is afdal (better), the passage explicitly says there is 'no harm' in other surfaces. Similarly, repeating surahs is permissible, though one may choose variety.
The afdal does not negate the permissibility; it is a recommendation for greater humility.
5
Apply the Hanafi position
State the mufta bihi: both actions are mubah (permissible). Some other schools may view praying on carpets as makruh, but the Hanafi school relies on the prophetic practice.
Note the cross-madhhab difference mentioned in the mukhtalaf detail.

Chapter on what is not disliked for the prayer. With the corner of his eyes without turning the face. (592) There is no harm in praying on carpets, spreads, and felt. And best is prayer on earth or on what grows from it. (593) There is no harm in repeating a surah in the two rak’ahs of nafl. ... Lexicon: muq: corner of the eye. Translation (592): There is no harm in praying on carpets, bedding, and felt; yes, prayer on earth and what grows from it is better. Explanation: Prayer on earth is better because it has more humility and submissiveness, but if one prays on a carpet, bedding, or felt, it is not disliked. (Abu Dawood) (2) Anas ibn Malik narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to visit Umm Sulaym and sometimes prayer would come and he would pray on our mat, which was a mat sprinkled with water. (Abu Dawood) These two hadiths show that praying on a mat and bedding is permissible. Translation (593): There is no harm in repeating a surah in the two rak’ahs of nafl. Explanation: If one recites the same surah in both rak’ahs of nafl, there is no harm. Another meaning is that if one recites two surahs in one rak’ah, there is also no harm, because one may lengthen his prayer as he wishes. Evidence: (1) Mu’adh ibn ‘Abdillah al-Juhani reported that a man from Juhaynah told him that he heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) recite in Fajr ‘Idha zulzilati al-ardu’ in both rak’ahs, so I do not know if the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forgot or did that intentionally. (Muslim) This hadith shows that in Tahajjud prayer, one rak’ah (the text cuts off).

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi tradition. It addresses two actions that are not disliked in prayer. First: praying on carpets, bedding, or felt is permissible (mubah), though praying on the ground or on natural plant materials is superior (afdal) for greater humility. The hadith of Maimunah and Anas confirm that the Prophet prayed on mats and bedding. Second: repeating the same surah in both rak’ahs of nafl prayer is permissible, as is reciting multiple surahs in one rak’ah. This is based on the practice of the Prophet, as reported by Mu’adh and Hudhayfah, showing flexibility in nafl worship. The Hanafi school follows these proofs, considering these actions not makruh.

When Breaking Obligatory Prayer Becomes Wajib or Jaiz
Ruling on obligatory and permissible reasons to break prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on breaking prayer for istighatha and parents, and apply the principle that saving life overrides continued prayer.

Core Idea
Breaking prayer to save life is wajib; for parents' non-urgent call, it is jaiz.

This passage from a Hanafi text clarifies a common concern: when is it permitted or even obligatory to interrupt an obligatory prayer? The key is the underlying principle that a valid prayer can be repeated. The rulings hinge on the degree of necessity: saving a life makes breaking wajib, while responding to a parent's casual call is merely jaiz.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between istighatha (a call for help from a distressed person) and a parent calling. Recognize that each has a different ruling.
Istighatha with life threat leads to wajib; parent's non-urgent call leads to jaiz.
2
Examine the proofs (Quran and Hadith)
The author cites Quran 8:72 and a hadith of the Prophet shortening prayer due to a child's cry. Understand how these proofs support the obligation to assist when life is threatened, and the permissibility to break for lesser hardship.
The Quranic command to help (istinzar) is general; the hadith shows prioritising relief of hardship.
3
Apply the principle of 'important matter'
The passage states a principle: 'It is permissible to break prayer for an important matter.' Determine what counts as important: life-threatening need makes it wajib; non-urgent parental call makes it jaiz; severe parental need makes it wajib.
The principle guides the ruling: the more urgent the need, the stronger the obligation to break.

فصل: فيما يوجب قطع الصلوة وما يُجيزه و غير ذلك

فصل : نماز توڑ نا واجب وغیر واجب کے بیان میں

ضروری نوٹ : یہ مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں کہ نماز توڑ دینے کے بعد دوبارہ پڑھی جاسکتی ہے، اس لئے جہاں تھوڑی سی مجبوری ہو وہاں نماز توڑی جاسکتی ہے۔

اصول : اہم چیز کے لئے نماز توڑنا جائز ہے۔

وجه : عن عمرو سمعه من جابر كان معاذ يصلى مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم يرجع فيؤمنا قال مرة ثم يرجع فيصلى بقومه فأخر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ليلة الصلاة و قال مرة العشاء فصلى معاذ مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم جاء يؤم قومه فقرأ البقرة فاعتزل رجل من القوم فصلی ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب تخفیف الصلاة ، ص ۱۲۳، نمبر ۷۹۰ ) اس حدیث میں تھکن کی مجبوری سے نماز توڑ دی، اس لئے جان جانے یار تم جانے کی مجبوری ہو تو نماز تو ڑسکتا ہے۔ ترجمه : (۵۹۴) اگر کوئی مظلوم نمازی سے استغاثہ کرے تو نماز توڑ دینا واجب ہے۔ ہاں والدین کے صرف بلانے سے (بے ضرورت ) نماز توڑ دینا واجب نہیں ( جائز ہے)۔

تشریح : نماز توڑنے کے بعد دوبارہ اس کو پڑھی جا سکتی ہے، اس لئے اگر جان کا خطرہ ہو تو نماز تو ڑ کر اس کی مددکرنا واجب ہے، مثلا نا بینا کنواں میں گر رہا ہو، یا کوئی پانی میں ڈوب رہا ہو تو اس کو بچانے کے لئے نماز توڑ نا واجب ہے ۔ اور والدین کو کوئی خاص ضرورت نہ ہو اور بلائے تو نماز توڑ نا واجب نہیں ہے، البتہ جائز ہے کہ نماز توڑ کر اس کے پاس جائے ، اور اگر انکو سخت ضرورت ہو تو پھر نماز توڑنا واجب ہے۔

وجه : (۱) و ان استنصر وكم في الدين فعليكم النصر الا على قوم بينكم و بينهم ميثاق و الله بما تعملون بـصـيـر . ( آیت ۷۲ سورۃ الانفال ۸) اس آیت میں ہے کہ مدد مانگے تو مدد کرو، اس کے اشارۃ النص سے معلوم ہوا کہ مجبوری کے وقت نماز توڑ نا واجب ہے (۲) عن عبد الله بن ابی قتادة عن ابيه قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اني لاقوم الى الصلاة و انا اريد ان اطول فيها فاسمع بكاء الصبى فاتجوز كراهية ان اشق على امه ابوداود شریف، باب تخفیف الصلاة
Chapter on what necessitates cutting the prayer and what permits it and other than that. Chapter: Regarding cutting prayer being obligatory and not obligatory. Necessary note: These issues are based on the principle that after breaking the prayer, it can be repeated; therefore, where there is a slight compulsion, prayer may be broken. Principle: It is permissible to break prayer for an important matter. Evidence: From ‘Amr, he heard from Jabir: Mu’adh used to pray with the Prophet (peace be upon him), then he would return and lead us. On one occasion he delayed the prayer, and led his people, and when Mu’adh prayed with the Prophet then came to lead his people, he recited al-Baqarah, so a man left from the people and prayed alone. (Abu Dawood, Book of Lightening Prayer) This hadith shows that due to fatigue, prayer was broken, so if there is compulsion of life or death, one may break prayer. Translation (594): If a distressed person seeks help from the one praying, then breaking the prayer is obligatory. However, merely being called by parents (without necessity) does not make breaking prayer obligatory (it is permissible). Explanation: After breaking the prayer, it can be repeated, so if there is danger to life, it is obligatory to break prayer to help, e.g., a blind person falling into a well, or someone drowning in water, then breaking prayer to save him is obligatory. And if parents call without any specific need, breaking prayer is not obligatory, but it is permissible to break and go to them. If they have a severe need, then breaking prayer is wajib. Evidence: (1) 'And if they seek help from you in the religion, then help is required upon you except against a people with whom you have a treaty. And Allah sees what you do.' (Surah al-Anfal, verse 72) This verse indicates that when help is sought, you must help; from its indication of the text, it is understood that at the time of compulsion, breaking prayer is obligatory. (2) From ‘Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada from his father: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: I stand for prayer and intend to lengthen it, but then I hear the crying of a child, so I shorten it, disliking to cause hardship for his mother. (Abu Dawood, Book of Lightening Prayer)
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage provides rulings on when it is obligatory or permissible to break an obligatory prayer. The Hanafi school bases these rulings on the principle that a valid prayer can be repeated if broken for a valid reason. The key ruling: if a person in distress (e.g., blind falling into well) calls for help, it becomes wajib (obligatory) to break the prayer and assist. Evidence is from Qur'an 8:72, which obligates help, and the principle that saving life takes precedence over the prayer at that moment. For parents: if they call without urgent need, it is not wajib but permissible to break and respond; if they have a severe need, it becomes wajib. The hadith of the Prophet shortening prayer due to child's cry shows that relieving hardship is prioritized. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the degrees of necessity, making some acts wajib and others only jaiz.

Key Terms
استغاثة (istighatha): a call for help, seeking rescue
ملهوف (malhuf): a distressed person, one in dire need of help

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is breaking prayer obligatory?
A) When parents call you
B) When a distressed person seeks help and there is danger to life
C) When you feel tired
D) When you want to speak to someone

Key Takeaway
Breaking an obligatory prayer is wajib when a life is at stake; for a parent's non-urgent call, it is merely permissible.
