Permissibility to Cut Prayer for Fear of Harm
Ruling on cutting prayer due to fear for life or property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the situations in which cutting or delaying prayer is permitted in the Hanafi school and distinguish between obligation and permission.

Core Idea
Saving life takes precedence over prayer; cutting is wajib when life is in danger, permissible when delaying suffices.

The Hanafi school permits cutting prayer when there is a genuine risk to life or valuable property. This ruling is based on the principle of preserving life (hifz al-nafs). This lesson examines the specific scenarios mentioned by classical scholars and the distinction between obligatory cutting and permissible delay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the text and note the three situations: fear of a wolf for sheep, fear of a blind person falling into a well, and fear of a midwife that the child may die.
2
Classify the ruling for each scenario
For each scenario, determine whether the text commands cutting the prayer immediately or permits delaying it. The text uses 'cut' for immediate danger and 'no harm in delaying' for non-imminent cases.
Immediate danger of death or loss → wajib to cut; mere concern → ja'iz to delay.
3
Extract the underlying principle
The common thread is preservation of life or property. The Shariah prioritizes saving life over performing prayer in its time, but the degree of obligation depends on the immediacy of the threat.
This is rooted in the higher objective (maqasid) of hifz al-nafs.
4
Apply the distinction to new scenarios
Consider other situations: a fire approaching a house with people inside, a child about to drown. Think whether the ruling would be wajib or ja'iz based on imminence.
The key variable is the likelihood and severity of harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٥٩٦) وخوف ذئب على غنم او خوف تردّی اعمي في بئر و نحوه و اذا خافت القابلة موت الولد والا فلا بأس بتأخيرها الصلوة وتُقبل على الولد
تشریح : یہ خوف ہو کہ بھیڑ یا بکری کھا جائے گا، یا یہ خوف ہو کہ اندھا کنواں میں گر جائے گا، یا دایہ کو یہ خوف ہو کہ نماز میں رہوں گی تو بچہ مر جائے گا تو نماز توڑ دے، کیونکہ جان بچانا ضروری ہے۔ اور بچے کے مرنے کا خوف نہ ہو اور دا یہ بچہ نکالنے میں لگی ہو تو اس مجبوری کی وجہ سے نماز وقت سے مؤخر کر کے پڑھنے کی گنجائش ہے، کیونکہ یہ مرحلہ اہم ہوتا ہے۔
لغت : ذئب : بھیڑیا۔ تردی: لڑھک جائے۔ القابلة : دائی۔
(596) And fear of a wolf over sheep, or fear of a blind person falling into a well and the like, and if the midwife fears the death of the child, then if not, there is no harm in delaying the prayer and attending to the child. Explanation: If there is fear that the wolf will eat the sheep, or that the blind person will fall into a well, or the midwife fears that if she remains in prayer the child will die, then she should cut the prayer because saving life is necessary. And if there is no fear of the child's death and the midwife is engaged in delivering the child, then due to this compulsion, it is permissible to delay the prayer from its time and pray later, because this stage is important. Glossary: al-Dhi'b: wolf. al-Taraddī: to roll/fall. al-Qābilah: midwife.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This ruling lists situations where cutting prayer is permissible: fear of a wolf attacking sheep, a blind person falling into a well, or a midwife's concern for a child's life. The commentary explains that saving life takes precedence over prayer, so prayer should be cut. If no immediate danger, delay is permissible but not cutting.

Key Terms
ذئب (dhi'b): Wolf; a predator that poses danger to sheep.
تردی (taraddī): Falling or rolling; risk of falling into a well.
القابلة (al-qābilah): Midwife; a woman who assists in childbirth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which situation does the ruling say it is permissible to delay prayer rather than cut it?
A) When a wolf threatens sheep.
B) When a blind person is near a well.
C) When the midwife is attending childbirth without fear of the child's death.
D) When the prayer is sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Cutting prayer is obligatory when life or significant property is in immediate danger; delaying is permissible when there is concern but no imminent threat.

Punishment for Lazily Abandoning Prayer
Ruling on beating and imprisoning one who deliberately misses prayer lazily

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi punishment for a lazy abandoner of prayer and explain who implements it and the evidence.

Core Idea
A lazy abandoner of prayer is beaten and imprisoned until compliance, but only by the Islamic ruler.

This lesson addresses a specific case: a Muslim who believes in the obligation of prayer but abandons it out of laziness. The Hanafi school prescribes a severe ta'zir punishment to enforce prayer, distinguishing this from apostasy. We will examine the ruling, its implementer, and the evidence from hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is intentionally abandoning salah out of laziness (kasal). The ruling is that the ruler must beat the person severely until blood flows and imprison them until they pray.
Laziness is distinct from denial; denial constitutes apostasy with a different ruling.
2
Determine who implements the punishment
The punishment is a ta'zir and must be carried out by the Islamic ruler, not by individuals. This prevents chaos and ensures proper authority.
Ta'zir punishments are discretionary and can be adjusted by the ruler.
3
Examine the evidence
The hadith of al-Rabi' ibn Sabrah commands teaching children prayer and beating them at ten if they refuse. By qiyas, an adult who abandons prayer deserves even more severe discipline.
The hadith is ahad and zanni, but sufficient for ta'zir.
4
Note the scope
The same punishment applies to abandoning the obligatory fast of Ramadan out of laziness.
The text explicitly extends the ruling to fasting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٥٩٨) وتارک الصلوة عمدا كسلا يضرب ضربا شديدا حتى يسيل منه الدم ويحبس حتى يصليها
ترجمه : (۵۹۸) اور جان کرستی سے نماز چھوڑنے پر اتنا مارا جائے گا کہ خون بہنے لگے، اور قید کیا جائے گا یہاں تک کہ نماز پڑھنے لگے، اور ایسے ہی رمضان کے روزے چھوڑنے والے [ کو مارا جائے گا ] تشریح : اور جان کرستی کی وجہ سے نماز چھوڑ دے تو اس کو اتنا پیٹنا جائز ہے کہ خون بہنے لگے، اور جب تک نہ پڑھے قید رکھا جائے۔ اسی طرح رمضان کا فرض روزہ ستی سے چھوڑ دے تو اس کو اتنا پیٹنے کی اجازت ہے کہ خون بہنے لگے ، اور روزہ رکھنے تک قید میں رکھا جا سکتا ہے۔ نوٹ : یہ کام حکومت اسلامی کا ہے، عام لوگ نہ کرے ورنہ انتشار ہونے کا خطرہ ہے، یہ دور وہ نہیں ہے۔ وجه : الربيع بن سبرة الجهني قال قال رسول الله الا الله علموا الصبي الصلاة ابن سبع سنين و اضربوه
(598) And the one who intentionally leaves prayer out of laziness is beaten a severe beating until blood flows from him and is imprisoned until he prays it. Translation: (598) For leaving prayer intentionally out of laziness, he will be beaten until blood flows, and imprisoned until he begins to pray, and similarly for one who leaves the fast of Ramadan. Explanation: If one leaves prayer out of laziness, it is permissible to beat him severely until blood flows, and he should be imprisoned until he prays. Similarly, if one leaves the obligatory fast of Ramadan out of laziness, it is permitted to beat him until blood flows and imprison him until he fasts. Note: This is the duty of the Islamic government; ordinary people should not do this, otherwise there is risk of chaos; this era is not like that. Evidence: Al-Rabi' ibn Sabrah al-Juhani said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Teach the child prayer at seven years and beat him...' (incomplete)
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage states the legal punishment for a person who deliberately omits prayer out of laziness: severe beating until blood flows and imprisonment until he prays. The same applies for missing the fast of Ramadan. The commentary adds a caution that this punishment is to be carried out by the Islamic state, not by individuals, to avoid chaos. A hadith about teaching children prayer is cited as evidence for the permissibility of beating to enforce prayer.

Key Terms
تارک الصلوة (tārik al-ṣalāh): One who abandons prayer; here specifically out of laziness, not denial.
كسلا (kasalān): Laziness; lacking motivation to pray despite believing in its obligation.
يضرب ضربا شديدا (yuḍrabu ḍarban shadīdan): Beaten severely; the extent is such that blood flows.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Execution.
B) Fine.
C) Severe beating and imprisonment until he prays.
D) Only verbal reprimand.

Key Takeaway
A lazy abandoner of prayer is punished by the Islamic ruler with severe beating and imprisonment until he performs the prayer, based on the hadith of teaching children.

When Breaking the Prayer Is Permitted
Listing situations that permit breaking or delaying prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five situations where it is permissible or obligatory to break or delay the prayer, and explain the Hanafi ruling on the one who deliberately abandons prayer out of laziness.

Core Idea
Necessity can override the obligation to maintain prayer continuity, but intentional laziness invites severe discipline.

The obligation of prayer is central, but Islamic law recognizes that preserving life and significant property may take precedence. This passage outlines specific emergencies that justify interrupting an obligatory prayer, as well as the serious consequences for those who abandon prayer out of sheer laziness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five emergency situations
The passage lists five scenarios: theft of a dirham's worth, fear of a wolf for sheep, fear of a blind person falling into a well, a midwife's fear for a child's life, and a traveler's fear of thieves or highway robbers. Recognize each and note whether it permits breaking or delaying the prayer.
The first four permit immediate breaking; the fifth allows delaying the prayer beyond its time.
2
Classify the ruling for each situation
Determine the hukm level for each scenario: most are mubah (permissible) to break, but the midwife situation is wajib (obligatory) according to the text. Understand the reasoning: preservation of life overrides the prayer.
The text uses 'يجوز' (ja'iz) for most, but uses 'اذا خافت القابلة موت الولد' implying obligation because of imminent death.
3
Analyze the ruling on the lazy abandoner
The passage describes severe punishment for one who deliberately misses prayer out of laziness: beating until blood flows and imprisonment until he prays. Understand that this is an imam's duty, not for individuals.
The proof is a hadith about teaching children prayer, analogized to adults.
4
Examine the proof (dalil) cited
The author references the hadith: 'Teach the child prayer at seven and beat him for it at ten.' This is used by analogy (qiyas) to justify corporal punishment for adults who abandon prayer lazily.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud; it is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
5
Apply the lesson to practical scenarios
Consider examples: a person praying and sees a thief stealing his wallet worth a dirham – he may break prayer. A midwife attending a birth during prayer time – if the child's life is in danger, she must break prayer.
The key principle: necessity (darurah) allows exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما يوجب قطع الصلوة) (۵۹۵) ويجوز قطعها بسرقة ما يساوى درهما ولو بغيره (۵۹۶) وخوف ذئب على غنم او خوف تردّی اعمي في بئر و نحوه و اذا خافت القابلة موت الولد والا فلا بأس بتأخيرها الصلوة وتُقبل على الولد (۵۹۷) وكذا المسافر اذا خـافـت مـن الـلصوص او قطاع الطريق جاز له تاخير الوقتية . (۵۹۸) وتارک الصلوة عمدا كسلا يضرب ضربا شديدا حتى يسيل منه الدم ويحبس حتى يصليها لامر یحدث ،ص۱۲۳، نمبر ۷۸۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بچے کے رونے کی وجہ سے نماز میں تخفیف کی جاسکتی ہے تو مجبوری کی وجہ سے نماز توڑی بھی جاسکتی ہے، کیونکہ اس کو دوبارہ پڑھی جاسکتی ہے۔
لغت : استغاثه : غاث، یغیث سے مشتق ہے، مدد طلب کرنا ۔ ملھوف : لہف سے مشتق ہے مظلوم، مجبور ۔
ترجمه : (۵۹۵) ایک درہم چوری ہو جانے سے اگر چہ دوسرے کا ہونماز توڑ دینا جائز ہے۔ تشریح ایک درہم کی اہمیت ہے اس لئے اسکی چوری ہونے کا خطرہ ہو تو چاہے اپنا درہم ہو یا دوسرے کا در ہم ہو نماز توڑنا جائز ہے ترجمه : (۵۹۶) اور بکری پر بھیڑیے کے خوف سے ، اور کنویں وغیرہ میں نابینا کے گرنے کے خوف سے، اور بچہ کے مرنے
کے اندیشہ سے دائی کو نماز توڑ نا واجب ہے۔ اور اگر اس کے مرنے کا اندیشہ نہ ہو تو نماز کوتا خیر کر کے بچے پر متوجہ رہے۔ تشریح : یہ خوف ہو کہ بھیڑ یا بکری کھا جائے گا، یا یہ خوف ہو کہ اندھا کنواں میں گر جائے گا، یا دایہ کو یہ خوف ہو کہ نماز میں رہوں گی تو بچہ مر جائے گا تو نماز توڑ دے، کیونکہ جان بچانا ضروری ہے۔ اور بچے کے مرنے کا خوف نہ ہو اور دا یہ بچہ نکالنے میں لگی ہو تو اس مجبوری کی وجہ سے نماز وقت سے مؤخر کر کے پڑھنے کی گنجائش ہے، کیونکہ یہ مرحلہ اہم ہوتا ہے۔
لغت : ذئب : بھیڑیا۔ تردی: لڑھک جائے۔ القابلة : دائی۔

میں رکھا جا سکتا ہے۔ نوٹ : یہ کام حکومت اسلامی کا ہے، عام لوگ نہ کرے ورنہ انتشار ہونے کا خطرہ ہے، یہ دور وہ نہیں ہے۔ وجه : الربيع بن سبرة الجهني قال قال رسول الله الا الله علموا الصبي الصلاة ابن سبع سنين و اضربوه
عليها ابن عشرة _ (ابوداود شریف، باب ما جاءعتی یو مرالصمی بالصلاۃ ص ۱۰۹ نمبر ۴۰۷ )
Chapter on what necessitates cutting the prayer. (595) It is permitted to cut it due to theft of something worth a dirham, even if it belongs to another. (596) And fear of a wolf for sheep, or fear of a blind person falling into a well and the like, and if the midwife fears the death of the child, otherwise there is no harm in delaying the prayer and attending to the child. (597) Likewise the traveler if he fears thieves or highway robbers, it is permissible for him to delay the time-based prayer. (598) And the one who intentionally leaves prayer out of laziness is severely beaten until blood flows and imprisoned until he prays it... (Urdu commentary follows explaining each ruling and mentioning a hadith about a child crying, and then a hadith from al-Rabi' ibn Sabrah al-Juhani about teaching children prayer and beating them at ten.)
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings (ahkam) on the permissibility of breaking or delaying the obligatory prayer due to urgent necessities. The author first lists five situations: (1) theft of a dirham's worth, (2) fear of a wolf attacking sheep, (3) fear of a blind person falling into a well, (4) a midwife's fear for a child's life, (5) a traveler's fear of thieves or brigands. In the first four, one may break the prayer immediately; in the traveler's case, one may delay the prayer beyond its time. The commentary adds that for the midwife, if there is no fear of death, delaying the prayer is sufficient. The ruling on the one who habitually misses prayer out of laziness is that the Islamic authority should beat him severely until blood flows and imprison him until he prays. The same applies to abandoning the fast of Ramadan. The author cautions that this is the duty of the Islamic government, not individuals. The proof cited is the hadith commanding teaching children prayer and beating them at ten, which implies a similar severity for adults.

Key Terms
قطع الصلوة (qat' al-salah): To prematurely terminate an obligatory prayer before its completion due to a valid excuse.
تارک الصلوة عمدا (tarik al-salah 'amdan): One who deliberately skips an obligatory prayer without a legitimate excuse, out of laziness or disregard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which situation is it wajib (compulsory) to break the prayer?
A) When a thief steals a dirham from someone else
B) When a midwife fears the death of the child
C) When a traveler fears highway robbers
D) When a shepherd fears a wolf will attack his sheep

Key Takeaway
Necessity permits breaking or delaying prayer in specific emergencies; the intentional abandonment of prayer out of laziness incurs severe punishment by the Islamic authority.

6 min
Capital Punishment for Denial of Prayer or Fast
Ruling on execution for abandoning prayer/fast: only if denial or belittling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a person who abandons prayer or fasting is executed, and explain the distinction between denial/belittling and lazy abandonment using the hadith of Abu Bakr.

Core Idea
Denial or belittling of prayer/fasting constitutes apostasy; laziness does not.

This lesson clarifies a critical distinction in Hanafi fiqh regarding capital punishment for abandoning prayer or fasting. While some may assume that any non-performance leads to execution, the Hanafi school limits it to cases of apostasy—i.e., when the obligation itself is denied or belittled. We will examine the evidence from the hadith of Abu Bakr and its qiyas application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (abandoning prayer or fasting) and what the initial ruling is (not killed unless denial or belittling).
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith of Abu Bakr from Sahih Muslim about fighting those who distinguished between prayer and zakat.
The hadith explicitly deals with zakat, but the Hanafi school applies it by qiyas to prayer and fasting.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith supports the ruling: Abu Bakr fought only those who denied the obligation of zakat, not those who acknowledged but delayed. This shows that denial triggers capital punishment, not mere non-performance.
The legal principle: juhud (denial) of an obligation known by necessity makes one an apostate.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that some earlier scholars (e.g., some Salaf) held that even the lazy abandoner is executed. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the hadith.
This ikhtilaf affects the practical application of punishment.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position (execution only for denial/belittling) is mufta bihi and considered stronger due to the explicit analogy with Abu Bakr's practice.
The authority is zahir al-riwayah and supported by ijma' on apostasy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۵۹۹) ولا يقتل الا اذا جحد او استخف باحدهما.
ترجمه : (۵۹۹) اور قتل نہ کیا جائے ، ہاں اگر انکار کرے یا کسی ایک کو حقیر سمجھے تو پھر قتل کر دیا جائے۔ تشریح : نماز یا روزے کا انکار کرے، یا اس کو حقیر سمجھے تو اس سے آیت نماز اور آیت روزہ کا انکار لازم آتا ہے، یا اس کی توہین لازم آتی ہے جس سے وہ آدمی مرتد شمار ہو گا اس لئے وہ قتل کیا جائے گا لیکن اگر نماز اور روزے کے فرض ہونے کا اقرار کرتا ہے،لیکن ستی سے نہیں پڑھتا ہے تو وہ مرتد نہیں ہوا اس لئے قتل نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
وجه : عن ابي هريرة قال لما توفى رسول الله الله و استخلف ابو بكر بعده ..... فقال ابو بكر و الله الا قاتلن من فرق بين الصلاة والزكوة فان الزكوة حق المال و الله لو منعونى عقالا كانوا يؤدونه الى رسول
الله القاتلتهم على منعه - (مسلم شریف ، باب الامر بقتال الناس حتی یقولو الا الہ الا اللہ ، الخ، ص ۳۲ نمبر ۱۲۴/۲۰)
(599) And he is not killed unless he denies (the obligation) or belittles one of them. Translation: And he is not killed; rather if he denies or belittles one of them, then he is killed. Explanation: If one denies the obligation of prayer or fast, or belittles it, then this entails denial of the Quranic verses on prayer and fast, or their disrespect, so that person becomes an apostate and is killed. But if he affirms their obligation but does not perform them out of laziness, he is not an apostate and is not killed. Evidence: From Abu Huraira: When the Messenger of Allah died and Abu Bakr succeeded him... Abu Bakr said, 'By Allah, I will fight whoever makes a distinction between prayer and zakat, for zakat is a right of wealth. By Allah, if they withhold from me even a rope they used to pay to the Messenger of Allah, I will fight them for withholding it.' (Muslim)
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage clarifies the limit of capital punishment for abandoning prayer or fasting. The author states that a person is not killed simply for leaving these acts out of laziness; execution is only for the one who denies the obligation (juhud) or belittles them (istikhfaf). The commentary explains that denial of the fardiyyah of prayer or fast amounts to denial of the Quranic text, which constitutes apostasy (riddah), and the apostate is killed. However, if one acknowledges the obligation but fails to act, he is a fasiq (sinner) and subject to less severe punishment (beating and imprisonment, as stated earlier). The proof cited is the famous hadith of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, who resolved to fight those who refused zakat, distinguishing between those who denied its obligation (apostates) and those who merely withheld it out of greed. This analogy (qiyas) is applied to prayer and fasting: denial leads to execution; mere abandonment does not.

Key Terms
جحد (juhud): Denial of an established obligation of the faith, specifically the fardiyyah of prayer or fasting.
استخفاف (istikhfaf): Belittling or showing contempt for a religious duty, which also indicates a denial of its sacredness and thus constitutes apostasy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a person killed for denying the obligation of prayer?
A) Because he is disobedient and must be severely punished
B) Because denial of a clearly established duty makes him an apostate
C) Because the ruler has absolute authority to kill any sinner
D) Because he must be forced to pray

Key Takeaway
A person is executed for abandoning prayer or fasting only if he denies the obligation or belittles it, because that constitutes apostasy; lazy abandonment does not warrant execution.

Witr Prayer is Wajib According to Imam Abu Hanifa
Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling that Witr is wajib, with proof and intra-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the status of Witr prayer and distinguish the proofs of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib for Imam Abu Hanifa, but sunnah for the Sahibayn – the same hadith read differently.

This lesson unpacks an important intra-Hanafi debate: is Witr prayer wajib or sunnah? The passage presents Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling that it is wajib, supported by a hadith, while the Sahibayn consider it sunnah mu'akkadah. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school arrived at its operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what Imam Abu Hanifa rules regarding Witr prayer. The text explicitly says 'Witr prayer is wajib'.
The ruling is given as number (200).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that Witr is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Sahibayn interpret the same hadith differently: they understand 'additional' as supererogatory (nafl), and they note the Prophet's occasional omission of Witr.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the word 'additional' (amaddakum) indicates that Witr is an increase to the fard prayers, implying it shares their importance and is thus wajib, not ordinary nafl.
The hadith is cited as primary dalil.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If Witr is wajib, missing it entails sin and requires qada (makeup). If sunnah, missing it is less sinful and qada is not required.
The later mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view, so qada is not obligatory.

ضروری نوٹ : نماز وتر کے بارے میں پانچ بخشیں ہیں [1] وتر کی نماز واجب ہے، یا سنت ۔[۲] وتر کی نماز ایک سلام کے ساتھ تین رکعت ہے، یا ایک رکعت ہے ۔ [۳] وتر میں دعاء قنوت رکوع سے پہلے ہے یا رکوع کے بعد [۴] دعاء قنوت پورے سال پڑھے یا صرف رمضان کے اخیر میں [۵] اور نمازوں میں بھی قنوت پڑھے یا صرف وتر کی نماز میں یہ پانچ بحثیں ہیں۔

تشریح : صاحبین کے نزدیک و ترسنت ہے لیکن امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک وتر واجب ہے۔

Chapter of Witr. Important Note: Regarding Witr prayer, there are five points of discussion: (1) Is Witr wajib or sunnah? (2) Is Witr three rak'ahs with one salutation or one rak'ah? (3) Is the Qunut supplication recited before or after ruku'? (4) Is Qunut recited throughout the year or only in the last part of Ramadan? (5) Is Qunut recited in other prayers or only in Witr? These are five discussions. Translation: (200) Witr prayer is wajib. Explanation: According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), Witr is sunnah, but according to Imam Abu Hanifa, Witr is wajib. Evidence: (1) Abu al-Walid al-Adawi said: The Messenger of Allah came out to us and said: 'Allah has granted you an additional prayer which is better for you than red camels, and it is Witr. He made it for you between Isha and dawn.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah) The meaning of 'additional' over the fard prayers is that it is as important as fard, but we do not consider it fard.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on Witr prayer and clarifies the Hanafi position on its legal status. The author first enumerates five disputed issues regarding Witr: its rank (wajib vs sunnah), its number of rak'ahs, the timing of Qunut, the yearly or seasonal Qunut, and whether Qunut is for Witr only. The specific ruling given here is that Witr is wajib (obligatory) according to Imam Abu Hanifa, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), consider it sunnah (emphasized recommended). The proof cited is a hadith in which the Prophet gives the glad tiding of 'an additional prayer' (salatan amaddakum biha), which Imam Abu Hanifa interprets as indicating that Witr is not mere sunnah but has a binding character akin to fard. The commentary explains that calling it an 'addition' to the fard prayers implies that it shares the same importance, although they do not elevate it to the level of fard. The hadith is from multiple sources.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, consisting of three rak'ahs according to the Hanafi school.
صاحبين (al-sahibayn): The two chief disciples of Imam Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf (Ya'qub ibn Ibrahim al-Ansari) and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fard (obligatory) like the five daily prayers
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) – the view of the Sahibayn
C) Wajib (obligatory but less than fard)
D) Nafl (voluntary)

Key Takeaway
Witr is wajib according to Imam Abu Hanifa but sunnah according to the Sahibayn; the operative ruling follows the Sahibayn.

Witr Prayer: Wajib or Sunnah? An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
States the wajib/sunnah dispute with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on Witr, explain the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and evaluate the proof for the wajib ruling.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib according to Abu Hanifa, but sunnah according to the Sahibayn – a difference that affects whether missing it is sinful.

Witr prayer holds a special place in the Hanafi school, but its legal status is not without internal debate. This passage outlines five key issues regarding Witr, the first being whether it is wajib or sunnah. Imam Abu Hanifa considers it wajib, while his two main students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), consider it sunnah mu'akkadah. Let us examine the proof and the reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Five Issues of Witr
The passage lists five areas of difference regarding Witr. Note them: (1) wajib vs sunnah, (2) three rak'ahs with one taslim vs one rak'ah, (3) qunut before ruku vs after, (4) qunut all year vs only last part of Ramadan, (5) qunut in other prayers vs only Witr. Our focus is on the first.
This lesson only covers the first issue.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
The passage explicitly states: 'Imam Abu Hanifa: Witr is wajib.' Wajib is a distinct Hanafi category between fard and sunnah; omission incurs sin but is not as severe as omitting fard.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider Witr to be sunnah mu'akkadah. In their view, missing it is not sinful, but it is a highly recommended practice.
4
Analyze the Hadith Proof
The author cites a hadith: the Prophet ﷺ said Allah increased for them a prayer better than red camels – Witr. The reasoning: the word 'increase' over the obligatory prayers implies it shares their importance, but since it is not called fard, it is classified as wajib.
Consider how the word 'increase' (أمد) is used as evidence for obligation.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
Although the Sahibayn's view is recorded, the Hanafi school predominantly follows Abu Hanifa's position. Therefore, the mufta bihi is that Witr is wajib. However, the Sahibayn's view is considered a valid concession in certain circumstances.

Chapter on Witr. Necessary note: There are five sections regarding Witr prayer: [1] Is Witr prayer wajib or sunnah? [2] Is Witr prayer three rak'ahs with one taslim or one rak'ah? [3] In Witr, is the qunut dua before ruku or after? [4] Should qunut be recited the whole year or only in the last part of Ramadan? [5] Should qunut be recited in other prayers as well or only in Witr? These are five discussions. Translation: (200) Witr prayer is wajib. Commentary: According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is sunnah, but according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is wajib. Proof: (1) Abu al-Walid al-'Adawi said: The Messenger of Allah came out to us and said: 'Indeed Allah has increased for you a prayer which is better for you than red camels, and it is Witr. He has made it for you between Isha and dawn.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah) The meaning of 'increased upon the obligatory prayers' can only be that it is as important as fard, but we do not call it fard, therefore we consider it wajib.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on Witr prayer with a note outlining five points of difference. The main ruling here is that Witr is wajib according to Imam Abu Hanifa, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it sunnah. The author provides a single hadith as proof: the Prophet ﷺ said that Allah has increased a prayer for them, which is Witr, and it is better than red camels. The reasoning is that the phrase 'increased upon the obligatory prayers' indicates that Witr is on the level of fard, but since it is not explicitly called fard, it is classified as wajib. The commentary also explains the term 'صاحبين' (Sahibayn) meaning Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms
صاحبين (Sahibayn): Refers to Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main students of Imam Abu Hanifa.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act whose obligation is established by a proof that is zanni (probable in transmission or interpretation); missing it incurs sin but does not reach the level of fard.
سنة (sunnah): An act regularly performed by the Prophet; performing it is rewarded, missing it is not sinful but blameworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Wajib

D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Witr is wajib according to Abu Hanifa (the mufta bihi), but the Sahibayn consider it sunnah; the hadith of 'increase' is used to support the wajib ruling.

Witr as Three Rak'ahs with One Taslim
States the ruling and provides four proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the method of Witr and identify the proofs from sunnah and ijma.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib as three rak'ahs with one taslim, proven by prophetic practice and consensus.

The method of Witr is a clearly established ruling in the Hanafi school. This lesson presents the core position and the evidence that supports it, including hadith and consensus, while also noting a practical concession for following an imam in the Haramain during Ramadan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the initial statement: 'وهو ثلاث ركعات بتسليمة' – Witr is three rak'ahs with one taslim. Understand that this is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
The ruling is about the method (kayfiyya), not the obligation of Witr itself.
2
Locate the four proofs
The passage cites four pieces of evidence: (1) hadith of Ali, (2) hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b, (3) hadith of Aisha, and (4) the consensus reported by Hasan al-Basri. Identify each as either sunnah or ijma.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
For each proof, determine how it specifically indicates three rak'ahs with one taslim. For example, the hadith of Ubayy explicitly says 'ولا يسلم إلا في آخرهن' – he did not say salam except at the end.
4
Note the concession
Read the note: in the Haramain during Ramadan, one may follow the imam even if he uses two taslims. Understand that this is a concession (rukhsa) based on hadith allowance, not the default ruling.
This concession does not change the preferred method for individual prayer.
5
Apply the ruling
Practice applying the ruling: if you are praying alone, you must pray three rak'ahs with one taslim. If you are in Makkah or Madinah in Ramadan following a Hanafi imam who uses two taslims, you may follow him.
The concession is specific to that context.

( ٦٠١) وهو ثلاث ركعات بتسليمة
تشریح : دورکعتوں کے بعد سلام نہ پھیرے بلکہ تین رکعت کے بعد سلام پھیرے۔
وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن علی قال کان رسول الله علي يوتر بثلاث يقرأ فيهن بتسع سور من المفصل يقرأ في كل ركعة بثلاث سور آخرهن قل هو الله احد - ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الوتر بثلاث ،ص ۱۰۶، نمبر ۴۵۹) 
(۲) عن ابي بن كعب قال كان رسول الله الله كان يقرأ في الوتر بسبح اسم ربک الاعلی وفی الركعة الثانية بـقـل يـا ايها الكافرون وفى الثالثة بقل هو الله احد ولا يسلم الا في آخرهن (نسائی شریف، باب ذکر اختلاف الفاظ الناقلین بخیر ابی بن کعب فی الوتر ص ۱۹۱، نمبر ۱۷۰۲/ مستدرک للحکام ، کتاب الوتر ، ج اول ص ۴۴۶، نمبر ۱۳۹ ار ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی ما یتقر فی الوتر، ص ۱۰۶، نمبر ۴۶۳ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب ما يقر آفی الوترص ۲۰۸ نمبر ۱۴۲۳ ) 
(۳) مسلم شریف میں حضرت عائشہ کی ایک لمبی حدیث ہے جس میں حضور کی تہجد کی نماز کا ذکر ہے۔ اس سے بھی پتہ چلتا ہے کہ آپ وتر تین رکعت پڑھتے تھے انـه سـأل عائشة كيف كانت صلوة رسول الله ؟ ... ثم يصلى اربعا فلا تسأل عن حسنهن وطولهن ثم يصلى ثلاثا (مسلم شریف ، باب صلوة الليل وعد در كعات النبی فی اللیل ص ۲۵۴ نمبر ۱۷۲۳/۷۳۸) 
(۴) عن الحسن قال : أجمع المسلمون عن أن الوتر ثلاث لا يسلم الا في آخرهن (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ۷۴ ۵ من کان یوتر بثلاث او اکثر ، ج ثانی، ص۹۱، نمبر ۶۸۳۳) 
نوٹ حرمین میں رمضان میں امام جماعت کے ساتھ وتر پڑھا رہے ہوں تو انکے ساتھ دوسلام کے ساتھ وتر پڑھ لینا چاہئے، کیونکہ حدیث میں اسکی بھی گنجائش ہے اس لئے اتنے بڑے امام کے ساتھ وتر کی جماعت
Chapter on Witr. (201) And it is three rak'ahs with one taslim. Explanation: Do not say salam after two rak'ahs, but say salam after three rak'ahs. Proof: (1) Hadith from Ali: The Messenger of Allah used to pray Witr with three rak'ahs, reciting nine surahs from the Mufassal, reciting three surahs in each rak'ah, the last of which was 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad'. (Tirmidhi) (2) Hadith from Ubayy ibn Ka'b: The Messenger of Allah used to recite in Witr 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la' in the first rak'ah, 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun' in the second, and 'Qul huwa Allahu ahad' in the third, and he would not say salam except at the end of them. (Nasa'i, Hakim, Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud) (3) In Muslim, a long hadith from Aisha mentioning the Prophet's night prayer: ... then he would pray four rak'ahs, do not ask about their beauty and length, then he would pray three rak'ahs. (Muslim) (4) From Hasan al-Basri: The Muslims have agreed that Witr is three rak'ahs, and one does not say salam except at the end. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) Note: In the Two Sanctuaries (Makkah and Madinah) during Ramadan, if the imam is leading the community in Witr, one should pray Witr with him with two taslims (i.e., in two parts), because there is allowance in hadith for this. Therefore, with such a great imam, the congregation of Witr...
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage establishes the method of Witr as three rak'ahs with a single taslim. The author provides four evidences: (1) Hadith of Ali showing the Prophet recited three sets of surahs in three rak'ahs. (2) Hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b specifying the surahs for each rak'ah and that he only said salam at the end, confirming the single taslim. (3) Hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet's night prayer including three rak'ahs, which indicates Witr is three. (4) The consensus (ijma) of the Muslims as reported by Hasan al-Basri. The note addresses a practical concession: in Makkah and Madinah during Ramadan, if the imam leads Witr with two taslims (i.e., praying two rak'ahs then one), it is permissible to follow him, as there is evidence for that form as well. This shows flexibility in following the local imam while maintaining the preferred method.

Key Terms
تسليمة (taslimah): The act of saying salam to conclude the prayer; here 'with one taslim' means one salam at the end of three rak'ahs.
قنوت (qunut): A supplication recited in Witr; though not the main topic, it is mentioned in the introductory note as one of the five issues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b cited in this passage, how many taslims did the Prophet perform in Witr?
A) Two taslims, one after two rak'ahs and one after the third.
B) One taslim only at the end of three rak'ahs.
C) One taslim after each rak'ah.
D) No taslim at all in Witr.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Witr is three rak'ahs with one taslim, but allows following an imam who uses two taslims in the Haramain during Ramadan.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Witr: Wajib and Three Rak'ahs with One Salam
Ruling and proofs for witr's wajib status and three rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on witr and explain the proofs that establish its wajib status and its form as three rak'ahs with one salam.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib, not sunnah: three rak'ahs with one salam, established by command and consensus.

In this passage, the author presents the Hanafi ruling that witr prayer is three rak'ahs with a single taslim at the end, and that it is wajib (obligatory). You will learn the specific proofs from the Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma that the Hanafi school uses to establish this ruling, and understand why the Shafi'i school differs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on witr
Identify the precise statement: witr is three rak'ahs with one salam, and it is wajib. Note the wording in the text: 'وهو ثلاث ركعات بتسليمة' and the argument that witr is 'haqq' meaning wajib.
The ruling has two components: the number of rak'ahs and the legal status.
2
Locate the primary dalil (proof) for wujub
Find the hadith: 'الوتر حق فمن لم يوتر فليس منا' (Witr is a right; whoever does not pray witr is not from us). This is cited from Buraidah. Also the command 'أوتروا' from the hadith of Ali.
The term 'haqq' and the imperative 'أوتروا' are key.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves wujub)
In Hanafi usul, the imperative form indicates obligation (al-amr yufidu al-wujub) unless there is a qarinah indicating otherwise. Also 'haqq' in shariah often means wajib. The text explicitly says 'الوتر حق يعني واجب'.
This is a zanni dalil (ahad hadith), so the level is wajib, not fard.
4
Examine the proofs for the number of rak'ahs and salam
The author cites the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b and others showing the Prophet prayed three rak'ahs and only made salam at the end. Also the consensus (ijma) reported from al-Hasan.
The hadith 'ولا يسلم إلا في آخرهن' is explicit.
5
Note the inter-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers witr sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib. They interpret the same hadith differently, arguing that the command for witr is not absolute due to other evidence, or that 'haqq' can mean sunnah mu'akkadah. The Hanafi response is that the command and the term 'haqq' establish wujub.
This ikhtilaf has practical implications (e.g., missing witr knowingly may be sinful for a Hanafi).

Source Text

الله
وجه (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن علی قال کان رسول الله علي يوتر بثلاث يقرأ فيهن بتسع سور من المفصل يقرأ في كل ركعة بثلاث سور آخرهن قل هو الله احد - ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الوتر بثلاث ،ص ۱۰۶، نمبر ۴۵۹) (۲) عن ابي بن كعب قال كان رسول الله الله كان يقرأ في الوتر بسبح اسم ربک الاعلی وفی الركعة الثانية بـقـل يـا ايها الكافرون وفى الثالثة بقل هو الله احد ولا يسلم الا في آخرهن (نسائی شریف، باب ذکر اختلاف الفاظ الناقلین بخیر ابی بن کعب فی الوتر ص ۱۹۱، نمبر ۱۷۰۲/ مستدرک للحاکم ، کتاب الوتر ، ج اول ص ۴۴۶، نمبر ۱۳۹ ار ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی ما یتقر فی الوتر، ص ۱۰۶، نمبر ۴۶۳ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب ما يقر آفی الوترص ۲۰۸ نمبر ۱۴۲۳ ) ان احادیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ تین رکعتیں وتر پڑھتے تھے۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ ایک سلام کے ساتھ پڑھتے تھے۔ کیونکہ ابی بن کعب کی حدیث میں ہے, ولا يسلم الا في آخرهن، (۳) مسلم شریف میں حضرت عائشہ کی ایک لمبی حدیث ہے جس میں حضور کی تہجد کی نماز کا ذکر ہے۔ اس سے بھی پتہ چلتا ہے کہ آپ وتر تین رکعت پڑھتے تھے انــه سـأل عائشة كيف كانت صلوة رسول الله ؟ ... ثم يصلى اربعا فلا تسأل عن حسنهن وطولهن ثم يصلى ثلاثا (مسلم شریف ، باب صلوة الليل وعد در كعات النبی فی اللیل ص ۲۵۴ نمبر ۱۷۲۳/۷۳۸) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ آپ وتر تین رکعت پڑھتے تھے۔ (۴) عن الحسن قال : أجمع المسلمون عن أن الوتر ثلاث لا يسلم الا في آخرهن (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ۷۴ ۵ من کان یوتر بثلاث او اکثر ، ج ثانی، ص۹۱، نمبر ۶۸۳۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مسلمانوں کا اجماع ہے کہ وتر تین رکعتیں ہیں، اور اسکے اخیر ہی میں سلام پھیرے۔ نوٹ حرمین میں رمضان میں امام جماعت کے ساتھ وتر پڑھا رہے ہوں تو انکے ساتھ دوسلام کے ساتھ وتر پڑھ لینا چاہئے، کیونکہ حدیث میں اسکی بھی گنجائش ہے اس لئے اتنے بڑے امام کے ساتھ وتر کی جماعت نہیں چھوڑنی چاہئے
Chapter of Witr (601) It is three rak'ahs with one salam. For this reason they consider it wajib. (2) From Abdullah ibn Buraidah from his father: I heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ say: 'Witr is a right. Whoever does not pray witr is not from us.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi man lam yutir, p. 208, no. 419; and Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab ta'kid salat al-witr, vol. 2, p. 659, no. 4460) From this hadith it became known that witr is haqq, i.e. wajib. (3) From Ali: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'O people of the Quran, perform witr, for Allah is One (witr) and loves witr.' (Abu Dawud, Bab istihbab al-witr, p. 207, no. 1416; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a anna al-witr laysa bi khatm, p. 103, no. 453) In this hadith there is a command form which indicates obligation. From this also comes proof of witr being wajib.

Translation: (601) And it is three rak'ahs with one salam.

Explanation: Do not make salam after two rak'ahs, rather make salam after three rak'ahs.

Evidence: (1) Hadith is: From Ali: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to perform witr with three, reciting in them nine surahs from al-Mufassal, reciting in each rak'ah three surahs, the last of them being 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad'. (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-witr bi thalath, p. 106, no. 459) (2) From Ubayy ibn Ka'b: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to recite in witr: 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la' in the first rak'ah, 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun' in the second, and 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad' in the third, and he would not make salam except at the end of them. (Nasa'i, Bab dhikr ikhtilaf alfaz al-naqilin bi khabar Ubayy ibn Ka'b fi al-witr, p. 191, no. 1702; Mustadrak al-Hakim, Kitab al-witr, vol. 1, p. 446, no. 1139; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a ma yuqra' fi al-witr, p. 106, no. 463; Abu Dawud, Bab ma yuqra' fi al-witr, p. 208, no. 1423) From these hadiths it is understood that he prayed three rak'ahs of witr, and also that he prayed with one salam, because in the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b it says 'and he does not make salam except at the end of them.' (3) In Sahih Muslim, a long hadith of Aisha mentioning the Prophet's tahajjud prayer: '...then he prayed four [rak'ahs] – do not ask about their beauty and length – then he prayed three.' (Muslim, Bab salat al-layl wa 'adad raka'at al-nabi fi al-layl, p. 254, no. 1723/738) From this hadith also it is understood that he prayed witr with three rak'ahs. (4) From al-Hasan: The Muslims have agreed that witr is three [rak'ahs], and one does not make salam except at the end of them. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab 74:5 man kana yutiru bi thalath aw akthar, vol. 2, p. 91, no. 6833) This narration states that the Muslims have consensus that witr is three rak'ahs and one makes salam only at the end of them. Note: In the Haramayn during Ramadan, if the imam is leading witr in congregation, one should pray witr with him with two salams [i.e., as he does], because there is also scope for this in hadith, so one should not leave the congregation of such a great imam.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that witr prayer consists of three rak'ahs with a single taslim (salam) at the end. The author first states the ruling (601) and then provides extensive proofs from hadith and consensus. The proofs include: (1) The command 'awtiru' (perform witr) from the Prophet ﷺ, which in Arabic indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul. (2) The statement 'al-witr haqq' meaning witr is a right and obligatory. (3) Numerous hadiths show the Prophet ﷺ prayed three rak'ahs with one salam, e.g., the hadith of Ali and Ubayy ibn Ka'b. (4) The consensus (ijma) of the Muslims on this. The commentary in Urdu explains the ruling and clarifies the widely held view. A note at the end addresses a practical issue: in the Haramayn (Mecca and Medina), during Ramadan, the imam may pray witr with two salams (i.e., in two separate sections), and the follower should pray with him to avoid leaving the congregation, as there is hadith evidence allowing this. So this ruling is the relied-upon position of the Hanafi school: witr is wajib and is three rak'ahs with one salam.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The witr prayer, a specific prayer performed after the night prayer, consisting of an odd number of rak'ahs (three in the Hanafi school).
حق (haqq): In this context, it means obligatory (wajib) as derived from the hadith 'al-witr haqq'.
وجوب (wujub): Obligation at the level of wajib, as opposed to fard. It is a binding requirement but based on zanni evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, what is the status of witr prayer?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib
C) Fard
D) Nafal

Key Takeaway
Witr is wajib in the Hanafi school, consisting of three rak'ahs with a single salam, established by the command of the Prophet ﷺ and the consensus of the Companions.
